Valid and Invalid Words for Marriage Contract
Ruling on valid words for marriage contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which words validly effect a marriage contract in Hanafi fiqh and explain why certain words are invalid based on the requirement of permanent ownership.

Core Idea
Marriage requires words that transfer permanent ownership; temporary or non-ownership words are invalid.

The marriage contract, like all contracts, requires a specific form of offer and acceptance. In Hanafi law, the words used must indicate a permanent transfer of ownership of the wife's reproductive capacity (bud'a). This lesson examines the five valid words and three invalid words, supported by Quran and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the valid words
From the matn, list the five words that validly contract marriage: nikah, tazwij, tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah. Note that all imply ownership transfer.
Tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah imply ownership of the entire body, which can be used metaphorically for the vulva.
2
Identify the invalid words
List the three invalid words: ijarah (rent), i'arah (loan for use), and ibahah (permission). These imply temporary or non-ownership.
Marriage is permanent, so temporary transfer does not suffice.
3
Understand the legal rationale
The key principle is that marriage transfers permanent ownership of the bud'a. Valid words express this ownership; invalid words do not.
Ownership (milk) is central. Ijarah, i'arah, ibahah lack milk.
4
Examine the textual evidence
The commentator cites hadith (Sahl ibn Sa'd) where the Prophet used tamlik, and Quran 33:50 using hibah. These show the validity of these words.
The hadith 'amlaknāka' directly proves tamlik. 'Zawwajtuka' proves tazwij.
5
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
Given a scenario, determine whether a word implies permanent ownership. For example, 'I give you myself' (hibah) is valid; 'I lend you myself' (i'arah) is not.
Focus on the linguistic implication, not just the speaker's intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينعقد النكاح بلفض النكاح والتزويج والتمليك والهبة والصدقة ) ولا ينعقد بلفظ الاجارة والاعارة والاباحة.

[۱۷۶۱] (۳۶) نکاح منعقد ہو گا نکاح کے لفظ سے اور تزویج اور تملیک اور ہبہ اور صدقہ کے الفاظ سے۔
ان الفاظ سے نکاح منعقد ہو جائے گا۔
(۱) نکاح کے ذریعہ بضعہ کا مالک ہوتا ہے۔ اور تملیک ، ہبہ اور صدقہ کے ذریعہ پورے جسم کا مالک ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے پورے جسم کی ملکیت بولکر ایک جز کی ملکیت مراد ہو تو جائز ہے۔ اس لئے تملیک، ہبہ اور صدقہ بولا مثلا عورت کہتی ہے کہ میں نے تم کو اپنے جسم کا مالک بنایا اور شوہر نے کہا میں نے قبول کیا تو نکاح ہو جائے گا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے مثلا تزویج اور تملیک کے لفظ سے نکاح کا ثبوت حدیث میں ہے۔ ایک لمبی حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے عن سهل بن سعد ان امرأة عرضت نفسها على النبي ... فقال النبي الله املكناكها بما معك من القرآن (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب عرض المرأة نفسها على الرجل الصالح ص ۷۶۷ نمبر ۵۱۲۱ر مسلم شریف ، باب الصداق و جواز کونه تعلیم قرآن الخ ص ۴۵۷ نمبر ۱۴۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تملیک کے لفظ سے نکاح منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے اذهب فقد زوجتـكـهـا بـمـا معك من القرآن (ب) ( بخاری شریف، نمبر ۵۱۳۲، مسلم شریف، نمبر ۱۴۲۵) اس حدیث میں زوجت کے لفظ سے نکاح کا انعقاد ہوا ہے۔ اور همه کے لفظ سے منعقد ہونے کے لئے یہ آیت ہے وامرأة مؤمنة ان وهبت نفسها للنبي ان اراد النبى ان يستنكحها (ج) ( آیت ۵۰ سورۃ الاحزاب (۳۳) اس آیت میں وہبت کے ذریعہ نکاح کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ ایک حدیث میں بھی اسب کے لفظ سے نکاح کا اشارہ ہے۔ وقال سهل قالت امرأة للنبی اهب لك نفسی فقال رجل يا رسول الله ان لم تكن لك بها حاجة فزوجنيها (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا کان الولی ھو الخاطب صے سے نمبر ۵۱۳۱) اس حدیث میں ہبہ کا لفظ استعمال کر کے نکاح کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ اور صدقہ بھی ہبہ کے معنی میں ہیں اس لئے صدقہ کے لفظ سے بھی نکاح منعقد ہو جائے گا۔
(۱۷۶۲ (۳۷) اور نکاح نہیں منعقد ہوگا اجارہ ، عاریت اور اباحت کے الفاظ سے۔ ا کوئی عورت مرد سے کہے کہ میں نے اپنے آپ کو آپ کے پاس عاریت پر رکھا ، یا میں نے اپنے آپ کو آپ کے لئے مباح کیا، یا میں نے اپنے آپ کو آپ کے پاس اجرت پر رکھا اور مرد دو گواہوں کے سامنے قبول کرے تو اس سے نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔
نکاح کا ترجمہ ہے ہمیشہ کے لئے شوہر کو بضعہ کا مالک بنایا۔ اور اوپر کے الفاظ میں مالک بنانا نہیں پایا جاتا ہے۔ بلکہ وقتی طور پر اجرت لیکر یا حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت انس فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک عورت آئی اور حضور کے لئے اپنے آپ کو پیش کرنے لگی۔ آپ نے فرمایا تم کو میں اس عورت کو مالک بنایا اس کے بدلے میں جو تمہارے پاس قرآن ہے (ب) جاؤ میں نے تمہاری شادی کرائی اس کے بدلے جو تمہارے پاس ہے قرآن میں سے (ج) کوئی عورت اپنی ذات کو حضور کے لئے ہبہ کرے ، اگر چاہے حضور اس سے نکاح کرے (د) حضرت سہل فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک عورت نے حضور سے کہا میں آپ کو اپنی ذات ہبہ کرتی ہوں۔ تو ایک آدمی نے کہا یا رسول اللہ! اگر آپ کو ضرورت نہیں ہے تو میری اس سے شادی کرادیجئے ۔
Marriage is contracted with the words nikah, tazwij, tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah, and is not contracted with the words ijarah, i'arah, and ibaha. (Commentary: ... extensive explanation with hadith and Quranic evidence ...)
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on which words validly effect a marriage contract. Five words are valid: nikah (marriage), tazwij (giving in marriage), tamlik (making ownership), hibah (gift), and sadaqah (charity). Three words are invalid: ijarah (rent), i'arah (loan for use), and ibahah (permitting use). The reasoning: marriage transfers permanent ownership of the wife's vulva (bud'a). Tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah transfer ownership of the entire body, so they can be used metaphorically for marriage. Ijarah, i'arah, and ibahah imply temporary or non-ownership, so they do not constitute a valid marriage contract. The commentary provides evidence from hadith (Sahl ibn Sa'd's hadith about a woman offering herself) and Quran (Surah al-Ahzab 33:50) showing that words like tamlik and hibah were used by the Prophet for marriage.

Key Terms
تملیک (tamlik): Making someone the owner; used for marriage by transferring ownership of the vulva
اجارہ (ijārah): Renting; paying for temporary use
عاریت (i'ārah): Loan for use without compensation
اباحت (ibāḥah): Permitting use; making something permissible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which word is NOT valid for effecting a marriage contract in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Nikah
B) Tazwij
C) Ijarah
D) Sadaqah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a marriage contract must be expressed using words that clearly transfer permanent ownership of the wife's reproductive capacity; temporary or permissive words render the contract void.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Words That Effect and Nullify Marriage Contract
Ruling with proofs on valid and invalid marriage words

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid words for concluding a marriage contract according to the Hanafi school, and state the proofs from Quran and Sunnah for each category.

Core Idea
Marriage is a contract of permanent ownership; only words that imply full and permanent ownership are valid.

In the Hanafi school, the validity of a marriage contract hinges on the specific words used. The school identifies five terms that properly effect a nikah and three that do not, because they imply only temporary benefit. This lesson unpacks the authoritative position and the textual foundations—from the Qur'an and hadith—that justify this classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of words
List the words that effect a valid marriage (nikah, tazwij, tamlik, hibah, sadaqah) and those that do not (ijarah, i'arah, ibahah). Recognize that the distinction hinges on permanence versus temporariness.
2
Trace the underlying principle for valid words
Each valid word conveys permanent ownership of the private part (bud'ah) either directly (nikah, tazwij) or indirectly through ownership of the entire body (tamlik, hibah, sadaqah). Understand that owning the whole includes owning the part.
Tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah are accepted by analogy to nikah.
3
Examine the dalil (proof) for each valid word
Locate the specific Quranic verse or hadith cited: the verse on hibah (Surah al-Ahzab 33:50), the hadith for tamlik ('I make you the owner of her'), and the hadith for tazwij ('I have married you to her'). Note that sadaqah is treated as synonymous with hibah.
The proofs establish that these words were used by the Prophet himself for marriage.
4
Understand why invalid words fail
Ijarah, i'arah, and ibahah denote temporary transfer of benefit (with or without rent). Since marriage requires permanent ownership, these words cannot create a valid nikah. The contract is batil (void) if used.
Temporary words do not make the husband a permanent owner of the bud'ah.
5
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Given any pair of words, determine whether they imply permanent ownership or temporary benefit. This principle can be extended beyond the listed words to any expression used in a marriage proposal.
The Hanafi school relies on meaning, not just fixed vocabulary.

Source Text

وينعقد النكاح بلفظ النكاح والتزويج والتمليك والهبة والصدقة) ولا ينعقد بلفظ الاجارة والاعارة والاباحة.
[1761] (36) نکاح منعقد ہو گا نکاح کے لفظ سے اور تزویج اور تملیک اور ہبہ اور صدقہ کے الفاظ سے۔ ان الفاظ سے نکاح منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ (1) نکاح کے ذریعہ بضعہ کا مالک ہوتا ہے۔ اور تملیک، ہبہ اور صدقہ کے ذریعہ پورے جسم کا مالک ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے پورے جسم کی ملکیت بولکر ایک جز کی ملکیت مراد ہو تو جائز ہے۔ اس لئے تملیک، ہبہ اور صدقہ بولا مثلا عورت کہتی ہے کہ میں نے تم کو اپنے جسم کا مالک بنایا اور شوہر نے کہا میں نے قبول کیا تو نکاح ہو جائے گا (2) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے مثلا تزویج اور تملیک کے لفظ سے نکاح کا ثبوت حدیث میں ہے۔ ایک لمبی حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے عن سهل بن سعد ان امرأة عرضت نفسها على النبي... فقال النبي الله املكناكها بما معك من القرآن (الف) (بخاری شریف، باب عرض المرأة نفسها على الرجل الصالح ص 767 نمبر 5121، مسلم شریف، باب الصداق و جواز كونه تعليم قرآن الخ ص 457 نمبر 1425) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تملیک کے لفظ سے نکاح منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے اذهب فقد زوجتكها بما معك من القرآن (ب) (بخاری شریف، نمبر 5132، مسلم شریف، نمبر 1425) اس حدیث میں زوجت کے لفظ سے نکاح کا انعقاد ہوا ہے۔ اور ہبہ کے لفظ سے منعقد ہونے کے لئے یہ آیت ہے وامرأة مؤمنة ان وهبت نفسها للنبي ان اراد النبي ان يستنكحها (ج) (آیت 50 سورۃ الاحزاب (33)) اس آیت میں وہبت کے ذریعہ نکاح کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ ایک حدیث میں بھی ہبہ کے لفظ سے نکاح کا اشارہ ہے۔ وقال سهل قالت امرأة للنبي هب لك نفسي فقال رجل يا رسول الله ان لم تكن لك بها حاجة فزوجنيها (د) (بخاری شریف، باب اذا كان الولي هو الخاطب ص نمبر 5131) اس حدیث میں ہبہ کا لفظ استعمال کر کے نکاح کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ اور صدقہ بھی ہبہ کے معنی میں ہیں اس لئے صدقہ کے لفظ سے بھی نکاح منعقد ہو جائے گا۔
(1762) (37) اور نکاح نہیں منعقد ہوگا اجارہ، عاریت اور اباحت کے الفاظ سے۔ ا کوئی عورت مرد سے کہے کہ میں نے اپنے آپ کو آپ کے پاس عاریت پر رکھا، یا میں نے اپنے آپ کو آپ کے لئے مباح کیا، یا میں نے اپنے آپ کو آپ کے پاس اجرت پر رکھا اور مرد دو گواہوں کے سامنے قبول کرے تو اس سے نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔ نکاح کا ترجمہ ہے ہمیشہ کے لئے شوہر کو بضعہ کا مالک بنایا۔ اور اوپر کے الفاظ میں مالک بنانا نہیں پایا جاتا ہے۔ بلکہ وقتی طور پر اجرت لیکر یا بغیر اجرت کے فائدہ اٹھانے کے لئے دیتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ الفاظ نکاح کے معنی میں نہیں ہیں۔ اس لئے ان الفاظ سے نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔ مثلا اجارہ میں اجرت لیکر تھوڑی دیر فائدہ اٹھانا ہے پھر چیز واپس دے دینا ہے۔ اور عاریت میں مفت تھوڑی دیر فائدہ اٹھانا ہے پھر واپس دے دیتا ہے۔ اور مباح میں بھی مفت تھوڑی دیر فائدہ اٹھانا ہے پھر واپس کر دینا ہے۔ تو چونکہ ان الفاظ میں مکمل ملکیت کا ثبوت نہیں ہے اس لئے ان الفاظ سے نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔
انمول ملکیت ہونے کے الفاظ سے نکاح منعقد ہوگا۔ تھوڑی دیر استعمال کے لئے دینے کے الفاظ سے نکاح منعقد نہیں ہو گا۔
Marriage is contracted with the words nikah, tazwij, tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah, and it is not contracted with the words ijarah, i'arah, and ibahah. [1761] (36) Marriage will be concluded with the word nikah and with the words tazwij, tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah. Marriage will be concluded with these words. (1) Through nikah, one owns the private part (bud'ah). Through tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah, one owns the entire body. So it is permissible to intend ownership of a part by saying ownership of the whole. Therefore, if one says tamlik, hibah, or sadaqah, for example a woman says 'I made you the owner of my body' and the husband says 'I accepted', marriage will be concluded. (2) There is indication in the hadith. For example, evidence of marriage with the words tazwij and tamlik is found in hadith. A fragment of a long hadith: 'From Sahl ibn Sa'd that a woman presented herself to the Prophet... and the Prophet said: I make you the owner of her for what you have of the Quran.' (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith shows that tamlik concludes marriage. In another hadith: 'Go, I have married you to her for what you have of the Quran.' (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith uses the word zawwajtu. For the word hibah, there is this verse: 'And a believing woman if she gives herself to the Prophet if the Prophet desires to marry her.' (Surah al-Ahzab 33:50) This verse indicates marriage through the word wahaba. In a hadith: 'Sahl said: A woman said to the Prophet: I give myself to you. Then a man said: O Messenger of Allah, if you have no need of her, marry her to me.' (Bukhari) This hadith uses the word hibah. And sadaqah has the same meaning as hibah, so marriage is concluded with the word sadaqah. (1762) (37) Marriage will not be concluded with the words ijarah, i'arah, and ibahah. If a woman says to a man: 'I placed myself with you as a loan (i'arah)', or 'I made myself permissible for you (ibahah)', or 'I placed myself with you on rent (ijarah)', and the man accepts in front of two witnesses, marriage will not be concluded. The meaning of nikah is to make the husband permanent owner of the private part. In the above words, making owner is not found; rather, it gives temporary benefit with or without rent. Therefore, those words are not in the meaning of nikah. So marriage is not concluded with them. For example, in ijarah, one takes rent and benefits temporarily, then returns the item. In i'arah, one benefits free temporarily, then returns. In ibahah, likewise, free temporary benefit, then returns. So since these words do not imply complete ownership, marriage is not concluded with them. Marriage is concluded with words implying full ownership. It is not concluded with words implying temporary use.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the words that validly conclude a marriage contract. The base matn states that marriage is concluded with the words nikah, tazwij, tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah, and not with ijarah, i'arah, and ibahah. The commentary explains that nikah and tazwij directly imply permanent ownership of the private part (bud'ah), while tamlik, hibah, and sadaqah imply ownership of the entire body, which includes the private part by extension. Thus, these words are valid. Proofs are adduced from hadith and Quran: for tamlik, the hadith where the Prophet said 'I make you the owner of her for what you have of the Quran'; for tazwij, the hadith 'I have married you to her'; for hibah, the verse from Surah al-Ahzab and the hadith about the woman who gave herself to the Prophet. Sadaqah is treated as synonymous with hibah. Conversely, ijarah (lease), i'arah (loan), and ibahah (permission) do not imply permanent ownership but temporary benefit, so they are invalid for marriage. The commentary emphasizes that the essence of marriage is permanent ownership (milkiyyah), not temporary use.

Key Terms
نكاح (nikah): Marriage contract, which implies permanent ownership of the private part (bud'ah).
تمليك (tamlik): Making someone owner, used here to mean giving ownership of the body in marriage.
هبة (hibah): Gift, used here to mean gifting oneself in marriage.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity, synonym for hibah in this context.
اجارة (ijarah): Lease/hire, implying temporary benefit for rent, invalid for marriage.
اعارة (i'arah): Loan for use, free temporary benefit, invalid for marriage.
اباحة (ibahah): Permission, free temporary benefit, invalid for marriage.
بضع (bud'ah): The private part of a woman; ownership of which is the essence of nikah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, which of the following words is NOT valid for concluding a marriage contract?
A) Nikah
B) Tazwij
C) Ijarah
D) Tamlik

Key Takeaway
Marriage is a contract of permanent ownership; only words that express full and permanent ownership are valid; temporary words render the contract void.

Marriage of Minors by Guardian
Ruling on validity of minor's marriage contracted by guardian

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the marriage of a minor thayyib by her guardian and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A guardian can marry a minor thayyib because she, like a minor bikr, lacks legal capacity to consent.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the marriage of minors by guardians, focusing on the contested case of a minor girl who has been previously married (thayyib). While both schools agree on the virgin minor, Imam Shafi'i restricts the guardian's authority over a thayyib. Let us explore the proofs and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the guardian can marry a minor boy or girl, whether the girl is bikr or thayyib.
The base matn states: 'ويجوز نكاح الصغير والصغيرة اذا زوجهما الولي بكرا كانت الصغيرة او ثيبا.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Shafi'i opposes the marriage of a minor thayyib without her consent, arguing that her previous marriage gives her experience and capacity.
Shafi'i's position is mentioned in the text: 'ن امام شافعي فرماتے ہیں کہ ثیبہ شوہر کے ساتھ رہ کر تجربہ کار ہو چکی ہے...'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i relies on the hadith 'ليس للولي مع الثيب امر' and the understanding that a thayyib can choose for herself.
The hadith from Abu Dawud is cited: 'ليس للولي مع الثيب امر واليتيمة تستامر وصمتها.'
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis interpret this hadith as applying only to adult thayyib, not minors. A minor thayyib still lacks the capacity to consent, so the guardian retains authority.
The commentary explains: 'وہ تو بالغ عورت کی بات تھی لیکن نابالغ لڑکے یا نابالغ لڑکی کی شادی کرائے تو چونکہ ان کو عقل نہیں ہے اس لئے بدرجہ اولی ولی کے نکاح کرانے سے نکاح ہوگا.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi, the guardian can marry a minor thayyib without her consent; in Shafi'i, the guardian must seek her consent even if she is a minor.
This difference affects the validity and enforceability of such marriages.

ويجوز نكاح الصغير والصغيرة اذا زوجهما الولي بكرا كانت الصغيرة او ثيبا.[1763] (38) جائز ہے چھوٹے بچے اور چھوٹی بچی کا نکاح جبکہ شادی کرائی ہو ان دونوں کے ولی نے چھوٹی بچی باکرہ ہو یا ثیبہ۔ ر چھوٹے بچے کی شادی ولی کرائے اس سے اس کا نکاح ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح نابالغہ بچی چاہے باکرہ ہو یا ثیبہ ہو ولی اس کا نکاح کرائے تو نکاح ہو جائے گا۔ اوپر گزر چکا ہے کہ ولی کو نکاح کرانے کا حق ہے۔ لا نکاح الا بولی حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ اس لئے وہ نکاح کرائے تو نکاح ہو جائے گا (2) وہ تو بالغ عورت کی بات تھی لیکن نابالغ لڑکے یا نابالغ لڑکی کی شادی کرائے تو چونکہ ان کو عقل نہیں ہے اس لئے بدرجہ اولی ولی کے نکاح کرانے سے نکاح ہوگا (3) بعض مرتبہ کفو اور اچھا خاندان مل جاتا ہے جو بعد میں نہیں مل سکے گا۔ اب اگر اس وقت ولی نکاح نہ کرائے اور بچے یا بچی کے بالغ ہونے کا انتظار کرے تو بچے یا بچی کو نقصان ہوگا۔ اس لئے بھی ولی کا نکاح جائز قرار دیا جائے (4) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ابوبکر نے اپنی نابالغہ لڑکی عائشہ کی شادی حضور سے کروائی اور ہو بھی گئی۔ عن عائشة ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم تزوجها وهي بنت ست سنين وادخلت عليه وهي بنت تسع ومكنت عنده تسعا (الف) (بخاری شریف، باب النكاح الرجل ولده الصغار ص 5133، مسلم شریف، باب جواز تزويج الاب البكر الصغيرة ص 456 نمبر 1422) اس حدیث میں چھ سال کی نابالغ لڑکی کی شادی باپ نے کروائی اور نکاح ہو گیا۔ ثیبہ لڑکی اگر نابالغہ ہے تو باپ اس کی شادی بھی کرسکتا ہے۔ چونکہ اس میں عقل نہیں ہے اس لئے باپ کو مدد کرنے کا حق ہے جس طرح باکرہ نابالغہ کی شادی کرانے کا حق ہے۔ نا امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ثیبہ شوہر کے ساتھ رہ کر تجربہ کار ہو چکی ہے اس لئے اس کی شادی کرانے کا حق ولی کو نہیں ہوگا۔ (1) اوپر کی حدیث میں عیب کو خود نکاح کرنے کا اختیار دیا گیا ہے۔ اور ثیب میں بالغہ اور نابالغہ دونوں داخل ہیں اس لئے دونوں کا نکاح نہیں کر سکتا (2) ابوداؤد میں ہے عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ليس للولي مع الثيب امر واليتيمة تستامر وصمتها.
حاشیہ: (الف) حضور نے حضرت عائشہ سے شادی کی اس حال میں کہ وہ چھ سال کی تھی۔ اور رخصتی ہوئی اس حال میں کہ نو سال کی تھی۔ اور آپ کے پاس نو سال تک ٹھہری۔
It is permissible to marry a minor boy and a minor girl when the guardian gives them in marriage, whether the minor girl is a virgin or previously married. [1763] (38) The marriage of a minor boy and a minor girl is permissible when their guardian marries them off, whether the minor girl is a virgin (bikr) or previously married (thayyib). If a guardian marries off a minor boy, his marriage will be valid. Similarly, if the guardian of a minor girl, whether she is a virgin or previously married, marries her off, the marriage will be valid. It has passed earlier that the guardian has the right to give in marriage; the hadith 'la nikaha illa bi wali' has passed. Therefore, if he gives in marriage, it is valid. (2) That was for an adult woman, but if he marries off a minor boy or girl, since they have no intellect, then by priority the guardian's marriage will be valid. (3) Sometimes a compatible match and good family is found that may not be found later. So if the guardian does not marry them now and waits for the child to become adult, the child may suffer loss. Therefore, the guardian's marriage is deemed permissible. (4) In hadith, Abu Bakr married his minor daughter Aisha to the Prophet and it happened. From Aisha that the Prophet married her when she was six years old, and consummated with her when she was nine, and she stayed with him for nine years. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, a six-year-old minor girl's father married her and the marriage took place. If a previously married girl is minor, her father can also marry her off. Since she has no intellect, the father has the right to help her just as he has the right to marry off a virgin minor. Imam Shafi'i says that a previously married woman is experienced from living with her husband, so the guardian does not have the right to marry her off. (1) In the above hadith, the thayyib woman is given the choice to marry herself, and both adult and minor thayyib are included, so he cannot marry her off. (2) In Abu Dawud: from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The guardian has no authority over the thayyib woman, and the orphan girl is consulted, and her silence is her consent.'
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage addresses the Hanafi ruling on the marriage of minors by their guardians. The base matn states that it is permissible for a guardian to marry a minor boy or girl, regardless of whether the girl is a virgin (bikr) or previously married (thayyib). The commentary provides several justifications: the general authority of the guardian supported by the hadith 'la nikaha illa bi wali'; the minor's lack of intellect, making the guardian's authority even more necessary; the potential benefit of securing a good match; and the prophetic precedent where Abu Bakr married Aisha to the Prophet when she was six. The text then presents the opposing view of Imam Shafi'i, who restricts the guardian's authority over a thayyib woman, arguing that her experience makes her capable of consent. The Hanafi response is that the hadith giving the thayyib the right to choose pertains to adult women, not minors, and that the minor thayyib still lacks capacity. The passage also cites a hadith from Abu Dawud that is used by Shafi'i but is interpreted by Hanafis as referring to adult women.

Key Terms
صغير/صغيرة (saghir/saghirah): A minor who has not reached puberty and is not legally capable of consenting to marriage.
ولي (wali): Guardian authorized to contract marriage for a minor, typically the father or closest male relative.
بكر (bikr): Virgin; a girl who has not been married before.
ثيب (thayyib): Previously married woman (non-virgin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a guardian marry a minor girl who has been previously married (thayyib) without her consent?
A) Yes, because the minor lacks capacity even if previously married.
B) No, because a thayyib always has the right to consent.
C) Yes, but only if she is a virgin.
D) No, only the father can marry a minor thayyib.

Key Takeaway
A guardian may marry a minor thayyib because minority, not marital history, determines capacity.

Marriage of Minors by Guardian: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on validity of marriage of minors by guardian with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the marriage of minors by a guardian and explain the proof from the Aisha hadith, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position regarding a minor thayyib.

Core Idea
A guardian may marry his minor ward because the minor lacks reason, as proven by the Prophet's own marriage to Aisha.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental rule of Hanafi family law: the guardian's right to contract marriage for a minor child. This ruling is grounded in the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the principle of guardianship (wilayah). We will also explore the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding a minor thayyib girl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Clarify that the marriage of a minor boy or girl by the guardian is valid (ja'iz). Note that the girl may be virgin or thayyib.
2
Examine the primary proof (dalil)
Study the hadith of Aisha's marriage. Identify it as a fi'l (action) of the Prophet, which indicates permissibility in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the dispute with al-Shafi'i
Understand that al-Shafi'i distinguishes between a minor virgin and a minor thayyib. Trace his proof (hadith about thayyib) and the Hanafi response (that hadith applies to adults).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: Hanafi allows father to marry minor thayyib; Shafi'i requires her consent at puberty. The relied-upon view is the Hanafi position.

Book of Marriage. (38) And the marriage of a minor boy and minor girl is permissible when the guardian marries them, whether the minor girl is a virgin or previously married. (Then Urdu commentary explaining that words indicating temporary benefit do not effect marriage, while words of complete ownership do. The ruling: it is permissible for a guardian to marry a minor boy or girl, whether the girl is virgin or thayyib. The preceding hadith 'no marriage without a guardian' was about adults; for minors it is even more applicable. Also, a suitable match may be lost if waiting. Proof: Aisha was married at six and consummated at nine. The father has the right to marry a minor thayyib girl because she lacks reason. Imam Shafi'i says the guardian does not have the right for a thayyib because she has experience. But the hadith of Aisha includes both virgin and thayyib; and there is a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the guardian has no control over a thayyib, and an orphan is consulted, her silence is consent.)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the validity of marriage of minors by a guardian. The author states the ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) for a guardian to marry off a minor boy or minor girl, regardless of whether the girl is a virgin (bikr) or previously married (thayyib). The commentary then explains that words implying temporary transfer (like ijarah, ariyah, ibahah) do not constitute marriage because they do not establish full ownership; only words of permanent ownership effect marriage. The guardian’s right is based on the hadith 'la nikaha illa bi wali' (no marriage without a guardian), and for minors this right is even stronger because they lack intellect. Additionally, delaying might cause loss of a good match. The primary proof is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) married her when she was six, and consummated the marriage when she was nine, and her father Abu Bakr was the guardian. This establishes that a father can marry his minor daughter. The author then addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that a thayyib minor girl cannot be married by her guardian without her consent because she has experience. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Aisha includes both virgin and thayyib; also, the hadith of Ibn Abbas indicates that for a thayyib (even minor) the guardian's control is limited, but the text here seems to differentiate: the author mentions the Shafi'i view and then presents a counter-argument. The Hanafi position, as stated, is that the guardian can marry a minor thayyib because she lacks complete reasoning, just like a minor virgin. The author concludes with the hadith from Abu Dawud: 'There is no authority for the guardian over a thayyib, and the orphan is to be consulted, her silence is consent' – but this is interpreted by the Hanafis to apply to adult thayyibs, not minors.

Key Terms
صغير (saghir): A minor boy who has not reached puberty.
صغيرة (saghirah): A minor girl who has not reached puberty.
ولي (wali): The guardian authorized to contract marriage, specifically the 'asabah (agnatic relatives) in order.
ثيب (thayyib): A woman who has been previously married (and thus not a virgin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on a father marrying his minor thayyib (previously married) daughter?
A) It is not valid because she has experience and must consent.
B) It is valid because she lacks complete intellect and the father's authority applies.
C) It is makruh but valid.
D) It requires a judge's permission.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows a guardian to marry off a minor child (boy or girl, virgin or previously married) because the minor lacks full reasoning, as proven by the Prophet's marriage to Aisha and the principle of wilayah.

Guardianship in Marriage: The Father and Grandfather's Binding Authority
Definition of guardian and exception for father/grandfather

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of a guardian in Hanafi fiqh, identify the order of guardianship, and apply the ruling that a marriage contracted by the father or grandfather is binding with no option of annulment after puberty.

Core Idea
Father and grandfather are special: their marriage of a minor is binding and cannot be annulled after puberty.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition of the marriage guardian (wali) and a key ruling: when the father or grandfather contracts a marriage for a minor child, that marriage is final. Other guardians (brother, uncle, etc.) give the minor the option (khiyar) to annul upon reaching puberty. We will trace the proofs and rationale behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Define the guardian
Identify who can act as a guardian for marriage according to the Hanafi school. The guardian is the 'asabah (agnatic relative) in a specific order.
The order mirrors inheritance: father, then grandfather, then son, then brother, then paternal uncle, then cousin, then mother (if no 'asabah).
2
Identify the ruling on father/grandfather
Note that if the father or grandfather marries a minor, there is no khiyar (option to annul) after puberty. This is a special exception.
The ruling is general for both sons and daughters.
3
Locate the evidence
Find the proofs cited: hadith from Aisha about the order, hadith of Anas showing son as guardian, and athar of Umar about mother. Also note the rational proof (ta'lil): father has both affection and intelligence, making his judgment binding.
The proofs establish the order and the finality of father/grandfather's decision.
4
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains: the father (and similarly grandfather) possesses shafaqah (affection) and 'aql (intelligence). Therefore his choice is in the child's best interest and cannot be undone.
This 'illa differentiates father/grandfather from other guardians.
5
Apply the ruling
Test different scenarios: if a brother marries a minor girl, she gets khiyar; if father marries, no khiyar. Recognize the practical implication.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh.

۱۷۶۴ (۳۹) والولى هو العصبة [ ۱۷۶۵ (۴۰) فان زوجهما الاب او الجد فلا خيار لهما بعد البلوغ.

جس ترتیب میں وراثت میں عصبات کو حق وراثت ملتا ہے اسی ترتیب سے نکاح کرانے میں بھی نکاح کرانے کا حق ہے۔ اس کی ترتیب اس طرح ہوگی۔ پہلے باپ کو نکاح کرانے کا حق ہے۔ وہ نہ ہو تو دادا کو ، وہ نہ ہو تو بیٹے کو، وہ نہ ہو تو بھائی کو ، وہ نہ ہو تو چا کو اور وہ نہ ہو تو چچازاد بھائی کو اور وہ بھی نہ ہو تو ماں کو نکاح کرانے کا حق ہوتا ہے۔
ولی کے سلسلے میں یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الله ... فان تشاجروا فالسلطان ولى من لا ولى له (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الولی ص ۲۹۱ نمبر ۲۰۸۳ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء لا نکاح الا بولی ص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۰۲ ارنسائی شریف ، نمبر ۵۳۹۴) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ ولایت میں ترتیب ہے اور جس کا ولی نہ ہو اس کا ولی سلطان ہے۔ بیٹے کے ولی ہونے کے سلسلے میں ایک لمبی حدیث کا ٹکڑا ہے۔ جس میں حضرت ام سلیم نے اپنے بیٹے حضرت انس کو ابو طلحہ سے نکاح کرانے کے لئے کہا۔ عن انس ان ابا طلحة خطب ام سليم ... قالت يا انس زوج ابا طلحة قال الشيخ وانس بن مالك ابنها وعصبتها (ج) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب الابن یزوجھا اذا کان عصبته لها بغیر انوۃ ج سابع ص۲۱۳، نمبر ۱۳۷۵۵) اس اثر میں حضرت انس بیٹے کو نکاح کا ولی بنایا گیا ہے۔ اور کوئی نہ ہو تو ماں کے ولی بننے کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ قال عمر بن الخطاب اذا كان العصبة احدهم اقرب بام فهو احق (د) (رواه الامام محمد فی کتاب انج ص ۲۹۳ / اعلاء السنن، نمبر ۳۱۴۲) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی عصبہ نہ ہو تو ماں نکاح کرانے کی حقدار ہے۔
[۱۷۶۵) (۴۰) پس اگر ان دونوں کی شادی باپ اور دادا نے کرائی تو ان دونوں کو بلوغ کے بعد خیار نہیں ہوگا۔ اگر چھوٹے نابالغ بچے یا بچی کی شادی باپ نے یا دادا نے کرادی تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد ان کو اس نکاح کے توڑنے کا خیار نہیں ہوگا۔ اور ان کے علاوہ نے نکاح کرایا تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد توڑنے کا خیار بلوغ ملے گا۔ (1) باپ کو بیٹے کے ساتھ شفقت کا ملہ بھی ہے اور ان کے عاقل بالغ ہونے کی وجہ سے عقل بھی ہے۔ اس لئے مشفق اور عاقل نے نکاح کر ایا اس لئے ان کو نکاح توڑنے کا حق نہیں ہوگا۔ اور باپ نہ ہوتے وقت دادا بھی اسی درجے میں شمار ہوتے ہیں۔ اثر میں ہے عن عطاء
(39) And the guardian is the 'asabah. (40) If the father or grandfather marries them (the minors), then they have no option (khiyar) after puberty. (Then Urdu commentary: The right to marry is in the same order as inheritance of 'asabah: father, then grandfather, then son, then brother, then uncle, then cousin, then mother if no 'asabah. Hadith from Aisha: 'If they dispute, the ruler is guardian for one without a guardian.' Hadith of Anas ibn Malik shows the son is guardian. Athar of Umar: 'If any 'asabah is closer to the mother, he is more entitled.' Then explaining (40): If father or grandfather marries them, no option after puberty; otherwise they have option. Reason: father has affection and intelligence, so his decision is final; grandfather is similar.)
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings: first the definition of the guardian (wali) as the 'asabah (agnatic relatives), and second, that if the father or grandfather contracts a marriage for a minor, the minor has no option (khiyar) to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty. The commentary explains that the order of guardianship follows the order of inheritance among 'asabah: father comes first, then grandfather, then son, then brother, then paternal uncle, then cousin. If no 'asabah exists, then the mother may act as guardian, as indicated by the athar of Umar. The proof for the order is the hadith from Aisha where the Prophet said: '...if they dispute, the ruler is the guardian of the one who has no guardian.' Another hadith shows that Anas ibn Malik acted as guardian for his mother Umm Sulaym. For the second ruling, the reason is that the father (and similarly the grandfather) possesses both affection (shafaqah) and intelligence ('aql); therefore his decision is considered final and cannot be undone by the child after puberty. If any other guardian (e.g., brother, uncle) marries the minor, then the minor does have the option of annulment upon reaching puberty. This differentiation is based on the principle that the father's love and sound judgment make his choice binding.

Key Terms
عصبة (asabah): Agnatic relatives (male relatives through the male line) who inherit after Quranic shares; here, the same order applies for guardianship in marriage.
خیار (khiyar): The option to annul a marriage after reaching puberty; only available if the guardian was not the father or grandfather.
بلوغ (bulugh): The age of puberty; for Hanafis, it is the onset of physical signs or reaching 15 lunar years.
شفقة (shafaqah): Tender affection and care, specifically the natural love of a father (or grandfather) for his child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, if a minor girl is married by her paternal grandfather, what is the child's right after reaching puberty?
A) She has the option (khiyar) to annul the marriage.
B) She has no option and the marriage is binding.
C) She must obtain the grandfather's permission to stay married.
D) The marriage becomes invalid automatically.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the father and grandfather are unique: their marriage of a minor is binding and cannot be annulled after puberty.

The Wali in Marriage: Hierarchy of the 'Asabah
Defining the wali and setting the hierarchy of guardians in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of marriage guardians (wali) and identify the proof for each level from the hadith and athar.

Core Idea
The wali in marriage is the 'asabah, in the order of inheritance; in their absence, the mother acts as wali.

This passage defines the wali (guardian) in marriage according to the Hanafi school. It establishes that the wali must be an 'asabah (agnatic relative) and specifies the order of priority: father, grandfather, son, brother, paternal uncle, paternal cousin, and finally the mother. The text supports each ruling with hadith and athar, demonstrating the evidentiary basis for the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the definition: the wali is the 'asabah. State the order of priority as given in the text.
The order mirrors the inheritance order of 'asabah.
2
Analyze the first proof: Hadith of 'A'ishah
Examine the hadith: 'If they dispute, then the sultan is the wali of the one who has no wali.' Understand that this proves the necessity of a wali and establishes the sultan as a fallback.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Nasa'i.
3
Analyze the second proof: Hadith of Anas and Umm Sulaym
Review the story where Anas ibn Malik, the son, acted as wali for his mother Umm Sulaym. This shows that a son can be a wali.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
4
Analyze the third proof: Saying of 'Umar
Consider 'Umar's statement: 'If any of the 'asabah is nearer to the mother, then he is more entitled.' This supports the mother as wali when no 'asabah exists.
The athar is narrated by Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Athar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1764] (39) ولی وہ عصبہ ہے۔ جس ترتیب میں وراثت میں عصبات کو حق وراثت ملتا ہے اسی ترتیب سے نکاح کرانے میں بھی نکاح کرانے کا حق ہے۔ اس کی ترتیب اس طرح ہوگی۔ پہلے باپ کو نکاح کرانے کا حق ہے۔ وہ نہ ہو تو دادا کو، وہ نہ ہو تو بیٹے کو، وہ نہ ہو تو بھائی کو، وہ نہ ہو تو چچا کو اور وہ نہ ہو تو چچازاد بھائی کو اور وہ بھی نہ ہو تو ماں کو نکاح کرانے کا حق ہوتا ہے۔ ولی کے سلسلے میں یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الله ... فان تشاجروا فالسلطان ولى من لا ولى له (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الولی ص ۲۹۱ نمبر ۲۰۸۳ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء لا نکاح الا بولی ص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۰۲ ارنسائی شریف، نمبر ۵۳۹۴) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ ولایت میں ترتیب ہے اور جس کا ولی نہ ہو اس کا ولی سلطان ہے۔ بیٹے کے ولی ہونے کے سلسلے میں ایک لمبی حدیث کا ٹکڑا ہے۔ جس میں حضرت ام سلیم نے اپنے بیٹے حضرت انس کو ابو طلحہ سے نکاح کرانے کے لئے کہا۔ عن انس ان ابا طلحة خطب ام سليم ... قالت يا انس زوج ابا طلحة قال الشيخ وانس بن مالك ابنها وعصبتها (ج) (سنن للبیہقی، باب الابن یزوجھا اذا کان عصبته لها بغير انوۃ ج سابع ص۲۱۳، نمبر ۱۳۷۵۵) اس اثر میں حضرت انس بیٹے کو نکاح کا ولی بنایا گیا ہے۔ اور کوئی نہ ہو تو ماں کے ولی بننے کے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ قال عمر بن الخطاب اذا كان العصبة احدهم اقرب بام فهو احق (د) (رواه الامام محمد فی کتاب انج ص ۲۹۳ / اعلاء السنن، نمبر ۳۱۴۲) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی عصبہ نہ ہو تو ماں نکاح کرانے کی حقدار ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا ولی کے لئے شیبہ کے ساتھ کوئی معاملہ نہیں ہے۔ اور قیمہ سے مشورہ لیا جائے گا۔ اور اس کا چپ رہنا اس کا اقرار کرتا ہے ( ب ) آپ نے فرمایا پس اگر وہ جھگڑا کریں تو سلطان اس کا ولی ہے جس کا کوئی ولی نہ ہو (ج) حضرت انس سے روایت ہے کہ ابوطلحہ نے ام سلیم کو پیغام نکاح دیا۔ حضرت ام سلیم نے فرمایا اے انس ! ابو طلحہ سے نکاح کرا دو۔ شیخ نے فرمایا انس بن مالک اس کا بیٹا تھا اور اس کا عصبہ بھی تھا (1) حضرت عمر نے فرمایا اگران میں سے کوئی عصبہ ماں سے زیادہ قریب ہو تو وہ زیادہ حقدار ہے۔
1764 (39) The wali is the 'asabah. In the order that the 'asabah inherit, in that order they have the right to perform marriage. The order is as follows: first the father has the right to perform marriage, if not present then the grandfather, then the son, then the brother, then the paternal uncle, then the paternal cousin, and if none of them exist, then the mother has the right to perform marriage. Regarding the wali, there is this hadith: From 'A'ishah, she said: The Messenger of Allah said: ... 'If they dispute, then the sultan is the wali of the one who has no wali.' (b) (Abu Dawud Sharif, Bab al-Wali, p. 291, no. 2083; Tirmidhi Sharif, Bab ma Ja'a la Nikah illa bi Wali, p. 208, no. 102; Nasa'i Sharif, no. 5394). From this hadith it is understood that there is an order in guardianship, and the one who has no wali, his wali is the sultan. Concerning the son being a wali, there is a portion of a long hadith in which Umm Sulaym told her son Anas to marry her to Abu Talhah: From Anas that Abu Talhah proposed to Umm Sulaym... She said: 'O Anas, perform the marriage contract with Abu Talhah.' The shaykh said: 'Anas ibn Malik was her son and her 'asabah.' (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Ibn yuzawwijuha idha kana 'asabataha la bi-ghayr inuah, vol. 7, p. 213, no. 13755). In this athar, Anas, the son, is made the wali of marriage. And for the case where no one exists, the mother becoming wali, there is this athar: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'If any of the 'asabah is nearer to the mother, then he is more entitled.' (d) (Narrated by Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Athar, p. 293 / I'la al-Sunan, no. 3142). From this it is understood that if there is no 'asabah, then the mother is entitled to perform the marriage. Footnote: (a) He said: The wali has no dealing with the virgin; and the mother will be consulted, and her silence is her consent. (b) He said: So if they dispute, the sultan is the wali of the one who has no wali. (c) From Anas: Abu Talhah proposed to Umm Sulaym... She said: O Anas, perform the marriage contract with Abu Talhah. The shaykh said: Anas ibn Malik was her son and her 'asabah. (d) 'Umar said: If any of them is an 'asabah nearer to the mother, then he is more entitled.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof. It defines the wali (guardian) in marriage as the 'asabah (agnatic heir). The author explains the order of priority: father, grandfather, son, brother, paternal uncle, paternal cousin, and in their absence, the mother. This order mirrors the inheritance order of 'asabah. The proof is provided through multiple hadith: the hadith of Aisha establishes that the sultan is the wali for one without a guardian; the hadith of Anas and Umm Sulaym shows that the son can act as wali; and the saying of Umar establishes the mother's entitlement when no 'asabah exists. The hashia provides further detail: the wali cannot force a virgin, her silence indicates consent, and the nearest 'asabah to the mother takes precedence. This clarifies the Hanafi position on the hierarchy of marriage guardians.

Key Terms
الولى (al-wali): The guardian in marriage, who is the 'asabah (agnatic relative).
العصبة (al-'asabah): Agnatic relatives who inherit through male lineage, in a specific order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The grandfather
D) The son

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi wali must be an 'asabah in the order of inheritance; only when no 'asabah exists does the mother become wali.

No Option of Annulment After Puberty if Married by Father or Grandfather
Stating the rule that marriage by father or grandfather gives no khiyar al-bulugh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-bulugh when a minor is married by the father or grandfather, and explain the reasoning and proof.

Core Idea
If father or grandfather contracts the marriage, the minor loses khiyar al-bulugh — their compassion and wisdom make annulment unnecessary.

In Hanafi fiqh, a minor who is married by someone other than the father or grandfather has the right to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty (khiyar al-bulugh). However, when the marriage is performed by the father or grandfather, this right is forfeited. This lesson examines the rule and its basis in the unique combination of paternal compassion and intellectual maturity, supported by an athar from 'Ata.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and note that it states no khiyar al-bulugh exists when the father or grandfather performs the marriage.
The ruling applies to both minor boys and girls.
2
Understand the exception
Contrast with the case where someone else performs the marriage — then khiyar al-bulugh is granted.
The word 'else' excludes father and grandfather only.
3
Examine the reasoning
The father combines compassion (shafqat) and intellect (aql); the grandfather is at the same level.
This dual quality ensures the marriage is in the minor's best interest.
4
Analyze the proof
The athar from 'Ata explicitly declares the marriage valid and that there is no option to divorce.
Although the athar mentions divorce, it is understood to mean no khiyar al-bulugh.
5
Note the scope
Only father and grandfather are excluded; other guardians (e.g., brother, uncle) do not share this status.
Thus, if such guardians contract the marriage, the minor retains the option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1734] (40) پس اگر ان دونوں کی شادی باپ اور دادا نے کرائی تو ان دونوں کو بلوغ کے بعد خیار نہیں ہوگا۔ اگر چھوٹے نابالغ بچے یا بچی کی شادی باپ نے یا دادا نے کرادی تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد ان کو اس نکاح کے توڑنے کا خیار نہیں ہوگا۔ اور ان کے علاوہ نے نکاح کرایا تو بالغ ہونے کے بعد توڑنے کا خیار بلوغ ملے گا۔ (1) باپ کو بیٹے کے ساتھ شفقت کا ملہ بھی ہے اور ان کے عاقل بالغ ہونے کی وجہ سے عقل بھی ہے۔ اس لئے مشفق اور عاقل نے نکاح کر ایا اس لئے ان کو نکاح توڑنے کا حق نہیں ہوگا۔ اور باپ نہ ہوتے وقت دادا بھی اسی درجے میں شمار ہوتے ہیں۔ اثر میں ہے عن عطاء
(حاشیہ  (1) حضرت عطاء نے فرمایا آدمی نے اپنے چھوٹے بچے کا نکاح کرایا تو اس کا نکاح جائز ہے اور اس کو طلاق لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہے یعنی خیار بلوغ نہیں ہے۔
1734 (40) So if the father or grandfather performs the marriage of these two, then for those two there will be no option after puberty. If a minor boy or girl is married by the father or grandfather, after reaching puberty they will have no option to annul this marriage. And if someone other than them performs the marriage, then after reaching puberty they will have the option of annulment (khiyar al-bulugh). (1) The father has both a quality of compassion towards his son and, due to him being of mature mind, wisdom. So a compassionate and wise person performed the marriage; therefore, they will not have the right to annul. And in the absence of the father, the grandfather is counted at the same level. In the athar from 'Ata: (Footnote (1) 'Ata said: A man married his young child, so his marriage is valid and he does not have the authority to divorce, i.e., no khiyar al-bulugh.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that when the father or grandfather marries a minor (boy or girl), upon reaching puberty the minor has no option (khiyar al-bulugh) to annul the marriage. The reasoning given is that the father (and grandfather) combine both compassion and intellectual maturity, ensuring the marriage is beneficial. The proof is an athar from 'Ata, which explicitly states that such a marriage is valid and the child has no right to divorce (i.e., no khiyar al-bulugh). This ruling applies exclusively to the father and grandfather, as other guardians do not share the same combination of qualities.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): Option or right to annul a marriage upon reaching puberty (khiyar al-bulugh).
بلوغ (bulugh): Puberty, the age at which a child becomes legally responsible and has the right to choose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Yes, if she is a virgin.

Key Takeaway
The marriage of a minor by the father or grandfather is irrevocable upon puberty; no khiyar al-bulugh exists.

Khiyar al-Bulugh: Option to Annul for Minors Married by Non-Father/Grandfather
Granting khiyar al-bulugh with Abu Yusuf's dissent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khiyar al-bulugh and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding its applicability.

Core Idea
A minor married by other than father or grandfather can annul upon puberty — except according to Abu Yusuf.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samari unpacks a key rule from al-Quduri: when a minor is married by a guardian other than the father or grandfather, the minor gains the right to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty. The sharh explains the rationale — such guardians may lack either full intellect (like the mother) or full compassion (like a judge or brother) — and cites supporting athar. Then it introduces a dissenting intra-Hanafi opinion from Imam Abu Yusuf, who rejects the khiyar relying on a different athar. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to navigate conflicting riwayat within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic rule from the matn
The matn states: if a minor is married by someone other than the father or grandfather, each minor has the option (khiyar) — they can uphold or annul the marriage upon puberty.
2
Understand the reasoning behind the rule
The sharh gives two scenarios: (a) guardian lacks intellect but has compassion (e.g., mother) — so she may not choose the right spouse; (b) guardian has intellect but lacks complete compassion (e.g., judge, brother) — so he may not prioritize the minor's best interest. In both, the marriage might be against the minor's interest, hence the right to annul.
3
Examine the textual evidence for the majority view
The author cites athar from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and Ibn Tawus, both indicating that minors married by a guardian other than father/grandfather have the option upon reaching puberty. These are dalil naqli supporting Abu Hanifa's position.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's dissent
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that even if married by other than father/grandfather, there is no khiyar al-bulugh. His proof is an athar from Hammad: 'The marriage is valid and she has no option.' The majority interprets this athar as referring to a case where the guardian is the father or grandfather.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: khiyar al-bulugh is established. This is the view found in zahir al-riwayah. Abu Yusuf's view is considered a weak (marjuh) opinion within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1766 (41) وان زوجهما غير الاب والجد فلكل واحد منهما الخيار ان شاء اقام على النكاح و ان شاء فسخ۔
نابالغ لڑکا اور نابالغ لڑکی کی شادی باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ نے کروائی تو ان دونوں کو خیار بلوغ ہوگا۔ یعنی بالغ ہوتے ہی اعلان کر دے کہ میں اس نکاح سے راضی نہیں ہوں ۔ تو وہ نکاح توڑ سکتے ہیں۔
(1) باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں یا تو قل ناقص ہوگی مثلاماں ولیہ بنے تو شفقت کاملہ ہے لیکن عقل ناقص ہے۔ اس لئے کہا جاسکتا ہے کہ صحیح جگہ پر نکاح نہیں کرایا۔ اس لئے نکاح توڑنے کا حق دیا جائے گا۔ اور قاضی، بھائی، چایا چازاد بھائی نے شادی کرائی تو ان لوگوں میں عقل تو ہے لیکن شفقت کا ملہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہا جاسکتا ہے کہ صحیح جگہ پر نکاح نہیں کرایا۔ اس لئے بالغ ہونے کے بعد نکاح توڑنے کا حق ہوگا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے کتب عمر بن عبد العزيز في اليتيمين اذا زوجا وهما صغيران انهما بالخيار. عن ابن طاؤس عن ابيه قال فى الصغيرين هما بأكيار اذا شبا (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیة التیمة تزوج وهى صغيرة من قال لها الخيارج ثالث ، ص ۲۴۸، نمبر ۱۵۹۹۵ بر ۱۵۹۹۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ یتیم کو اور قیمہ کو شادی کرائی۔ یقیمہ کے والد کا انتقال ہو گیا ہے اس لئے اس کے علاوہ نے ہی شادی کرائی ہوگی ۔ اس لئے ان کو خیار ملے گا۔
نانه امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ نے شادی کرائی تب بھی اس کو اختیار نہیں ملے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن حماد قال النکاح جائز ولا خيار لها (ج) (مصنف ابن ابى هيبة القيمة تزوج وهى صغير من قال لها الخیارج ثالث ص ۴۴۸ نمبر ۱۲۰۰۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ یتیمہ کوخیار بلوغ نہیں ہوگا۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ صغیر اور صغیرہ کو بھی باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ نے شادی کرائی تو اس کو اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔
1766 (41) And if someone other than the father or grandfather marries them, then each of them has the option: if they wish, they may uphold the marriage, and if they wish, they may annul it. 
If a minor boy and minor girl are married by someone other than father and grandfather, then both have khiyar al-bulugh. That is, upon reaching puberty, they declare, 'I am not pleased with this marriage,' then they can annul the marriage. 
(1) In the case of other than father and grandfather, either there is deficient intellect, for example, if the mother becomes wali, she has complete compassion but deficient intellect. Therefore, it can be said that the marriage was not contracted properly, so the right to annul is given. And if the judge, brother, paternal uncle, or paternal cousin performed the marriage, they have intellect but lack complete compassion, so it can be said that the marriage was not contracted properly, so after reaching puberty, they have the right to annul. 
(2) There is evidence for this in the athar: 'Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote concerning two orphans (male and female) when they were married while young, that they have the option.' From Ibn Tawus from his father, he said concerning two minors that they have the option when they grow up. (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, ...). This athar indicates that the orphan and the guardian were married (by someone other than father/grandfather), so they have the option. 
But Imam Abu Yusuf said that even if someone other than father or grandfather performs the marriage, he still will not have the option. His proof is this athar: from Hammad, he said: 'The marriage is valid and she has no option.' (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, ...). From this athar it is understood that the orphan girl does not have khiyar al-bulugh, meaning that a minor boy or girl, even if married by other than father or grandfather, does not have the option.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn (from al-Quduri) states that if a minor is married by someone other than the father or grandfather, the minor has khiyar al-bulugh (option to annul upon puberty). The sharh explains the reasoning: other guardians lack either full intellect (like the mother) or full compassion (like a judge or extended relatives), so the marriage may not be in the minor's best interest. The sharh also cites athar from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and Ibn Tawus supporting khiyar al-bulugh. Then the text presents Imam Abu Yusuf's dissenting view: he holds that even if married by other than father/grandfather, there is no khiyar al-bulugh, relying on an athar from Hammad that says the marriage is valid and there is no option. This is a clear intra-madhhab ikhtilaf. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the matn), granting khiyar al-bulugh, as most Hanafi works follow this.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option to annul a marriage upon reaching puberty, granted to minors who were married by a guardian other than the father or grandfather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, what right does a minor have if married by a guardian other than his father or grandfather?
A) No right to annul
B) Option to annul upon reaching puberty
C) Must wait until age 18
D) Can demand compensation

Key Takeaway
A minor married by a guardian other than father or grandfather has the right to annul upon puberty, per the majority Hanafi position, despite Abu Yusuf's dissent.

Who Cannot Be a Marriage Guardian (Wali)?
Listing those who cannot be wali and a related ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories disqualified from serving as a wali in Hanafi fiqh and explain the condition that a wali must be a free, adult, sane Muslim 'asabah.

Core Idea
A marriage guardian must be free, adult, sane, and Muslim — these four disqualify.

In Hanafi marital law, the validity of a marriage contract depends on the capacity of the guardian (wali). This lesson clarifies who cannot serve as a wali, drawing directly from the matn and sharh of the text. Understanding these disqualifications ensures that marriage contracts are sound and prevents invalid unions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal requirement
Recognise that wilayah (guardianship) in marriage is a condition for the validity of the contract, and it requires a specific capacity in the guardian.
The wali acts on behalf of the bride; a disqualified wali renders the contract void.
2
List the four disqualified categories from the matn
From the Arabic text: 'لا ولاية لعبد ولا لصغير ولا لمجنون ولا لكافر' — a slave, a minor, an insane person, and a disbeliever have no guardianship.
Each lacks a critical attribute: freedom, adulthood, sanity, or Islam.
3
Understand the underlying condition
These four share the absence of a necessary attribute: the wali must be free, adult, sane, and Muslim (when the bride is Muslim).
The condition applies cumulatively; missing any one disqualifies.
4
Analyse the sharh's expansion
The commentary adds: 'اذا انكح الرجل ابنه الصغير فنكاحه جائز' — a father may validly marry his young son (as wali), implying the father has wilayah over the minor son, but the minor himself cannot be a wali for others.
This clarifies that a minor can be the ward, but not the guardian.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a potential wali, check each condition: free vs slave, adult vs minor, sane vs insane, Muslim vs non-Muslim. If any condition fails, the marriage contract by that wali is invalid.
If no eligible wali exists, the qadi (judge) acts as wali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1767 (42) ولا ولاية لعبد ولا لصغير ولا لمجنون ولا لكافر انه اذا انـكـح الـرجـل ابـنـه الصغير فنكاحه جائز ولا طلاق له
غلام کے لئے ولایت نہیں ہوگی، اور نہ چھوٹے بچے کے لئے، اور نہ مجنون کے لئے، اور نہ کافر کے لئے مسلمان عورت پر ان لوگوں کو شادی کرانے کی ولایت نہیں ہوگی۔
1767 (42) And there is no guardianship for a slave, nor for a minor, nor for an insane person, nor for a disbeliever. [The sharh adds:] That if a man marries his young son, his marriage is valid and there is no divorce for him. 
For a slave, there will be no guardianship, and not for a young child, nor for an insane person, and not for a disbeliever over a Muslim woman; these people have no guardianship to perform marriage.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage defines who cannot be a wali (guardian) in marriage. The matn explicitly excludes four categories: a slave (due to his own lack of free will), a minor (due to lack of legal capacity), an insane person (due to lack of intellect), and a non-Muslim (due to lack of religious authority over a Muslim woman). The sharh adds a note: if a man were to marry his young son (i.e., as a wali) that marriage would be valid, but the father (if the matn implies father? Actually the Arabic phrase 'اذا انكح الرجل ابنه الصغير' is a conditional statement: if a man marries his young son (arranges his marriage), it is valid and the son has no right to divorce (i.e., no khiyar). This supports the previous ruling that father/grandfather have the right to contract marriage for minors without the minor having subsequent option. The passage affirms that these four categories lack the legal capacity (ahliyyah) to act as guardians.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority to act as guardian in marriage, specifically contracted to a free, adult, sane Muslim 'asabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) A minor
C) A Muslim father
D) A non-Muslim brother

Key Takeaway
A marriage guardian (wali) for a Muslim woman must be free, adult, sane, and Muslim; any marriage contracted by a disqualified guardian is invalid.

Marriage of Minors by Non-Father Guardians: Option of Puberty
Ruling on khiyar al-bulugh for marriage by non-father/grandfather

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on khiyar al-bulugh when a minor is married by a guardian other than father/grandfather, cite the athar evidence, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When a non-father/grandfather marries a minor, the minor gains khiyar al-bulugh — the right to annul upon puberty.

In Hanafi law, the father and grandfather have full marriage guardianship over minors. But when other relatives or the qadi marry the minor, the minor is not bound forever. This lesson examines the ruling that the minor has the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) to confirm or annul the marriage, the proofs from the traditions, and an important intra-Hanafi difference with Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the marriage of a minor by a guardian other than father/grandfather. The ruling: the marriage is sahih but the minor has the right to annul upon puberty (khiyar al-bulugh).
Contrast with marriage by father/grandfather: no option.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two athar: the letter of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz and the statement of Ibn Tawus, both indicating that minors have the option.
These are transmitted in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'huma bil-khiyar' (they have the option) directly establishes the ruling. The evidence is clear (qati' al-dalala) though the transmission is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: he holds that the minor has no option, relying on an athar from Hammad: 'The marriage is valid and she has no option.'
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the minor has the option. The majority of Hanafi scholars adopt this view.
The commentary does not explicitly tarjih but gives more weight to the prevalent view.

Source Text

And if someone other than the father and grandfather married them, each of them has the option: if he wishes he may remain in the marriage, and if he wishes he may annul. ... (then Urdu commentary and proofs)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage rules on khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) for minors married by a guardian other than the father or grandfather. The Arabic text states the ruling: each minor has the right to choose to keep or annul the marriage upon reaching puberty. The commentary explains that this applies when a male or female minor is married by someone like a brother, uncle, or qadi, because such guardians may lack either complete intellect or complete affection. It contrasts with the case where the father or grandfather marries the minor, in which case there is no khiyar al-bulugh. The passage then cites several athar (traditions) as proofs. Notably, it includes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that even when married by others, there is no khiyar al-bulugh, citing an athar from Hammad. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that when marriage is by father or grandfather, no option; by others, the minor has the option.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The right of a minor married by a guardian other than father/grandfather to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty.
ولایت (wilayah): Guardianship over a minor in marriage, held by father and grandfather (al-jadd) with authority to contract marriage without minor's consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a minor is married by a guardian other than father/grandfather, the marriage is valid but the minor can annul it upon reaching puberty — this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Who Cannot Be a Guardian: Slave, Minor, Insane, Non-Muslim
Ruling on disqualification of slaves, minors, insane persons, and non-Muslims from guardianship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of persons disqualified from acting as guardians in marriage and explain the legal reasoning, including the Quranic proof, for each.

Core Idea
Guardianship in marriage requires full legal capacity and faith; a slave, minor, insane person, or non-Muslim lacks this and cannot be a wali.

This lesson presents a clear ruling from the Hanafi school on who is disqualified from acting as a guardian (wali) in a marriage contract. The text lists four categories—slave, minor, insane person, and non-Muslim—and provides the underlying rationale, including a direct Quranic proof for the non-Muslim. Understanding these disqualifications is essential to ensure the validity of a marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is acting as a guardian (wali) in a marriage contract. The ruling is that a marriage contracted by any of the four listed individuals is invalid (batil) because they lack the legal capacity to be guardians.
The ruling is unanimous in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the four disqualified categories
The text explicitly lists: a slave ('abd), a minor (saghir), an insane person (majnun), and a non-Muslim (kafir). These are the only categories mentioned in this passage.
Other schools may add or differ, but these are the core Hanafi positions.
3
Understand the rationale for each
For the slave: lacks authority over himself (his master is his guardian). For the minor: lacks intellectual maturity. For the insane: lacks reason. For the non-Muslim: lacks faith, and Quran 4:141 denies any pathway for disbelievers over believers.
The commentary in the source explains each rationale succinctly.
4
Examine the proof for the non-Muslim
The proof is Quran 4:141: 'Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers.' This is a qat'i (definitive) text that establishes the prohibition absolutely.
The Hanafi school treats this verse as general and not subject to specification (takhsis) by reason or other texts.
5
Note the practical consequence
If a marriage is contracted by any of these individuals, the marriage is batil (void). It does not produce any legal effects, and the parties must separate immediately.
This differs from a marriage contracted without a guardian (which may be sahih under certain conditions).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۷۶۷ (۴۲) ولا ولاية لعبد ولا لصغير ولا لمجنون ولا لكافر انه اذا انـكـح الـرجـل ابـنـه الصغير فنكاحه جائز ولا طلاق له (الف) (سن للبیہقی ، باب الاب يزوج لبنه الصغير ج سابع مص ۲۳۲، نمبر ۱۳۸۱۷ مصنف ابن ابی هیسته ۱۲ فی رجل یزوج ابنه وهو صغير من اجازة ج ، ثالث ص ۲۴۹، نمبر ۱۶۰۰۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ باپ نے نابالغ بیٹے کی شادی کرائی تو اس کو طلاق دینے کی اجازت نہیں ہوگی۔ یعنی خیار بلوغ نہیں ملے گا۔ اور اسی میں دادا بھی داخل ہوگا۔ (1) ان لوگوں کو خود اپنے اوپر ولایت نہیں ہے تو ان لوگوں کو دوسروں پر ولایت کیسے ہوگی ۔ مثلا غلام کو اپنی شادی کرانے کا حق نہیں ہے۔ اس کی شادی اس کا مولی کراتا ہے تو اس کو دوسروں کی شادی کرانے کا حق کیسے ہو گا ؟ بچے کو عقل کی کمی ہے اس لئے اس کو دوسرے پر کیسے ولایت ہوگی ؟ مجنون کو بھی عقل نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کو دوسروں پر ولایت کیسے ہوگی۔ اور کا فرکو مسلمان پر ولایت نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ولن يجعل الله للكافرين على المؤمنين سبیل ((الف) ( آیت ۱۴۱ سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں ہے کہ کا فر کو مؤمنین پر کوئی راستہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کا فر کو مسلمان پر ولایت نہیں ہوگی ۔
There is no guardianship for a slave, nor for a minor, nor for an insane person, nor for a non-Muslim. ... (then Urdu commentary and proof from Quran 4:141)
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on who cannot act as a guardian (wali) in marriage. The Arabic text lists four categories: a slave (abd), a minor (saghir), an insane person (majnun), and a non-Muslim (kafir). The commentary explains the reasoning: each of these lacks either full legal capacity or faith. A slave has no authority over himself—his master is his guardian—so he cannot be a guardian over others. A minor lacks intellectual maturity. An insane person lacks reason. A non-Muslim cannot have authority over a Muslim, as per Quran 4:141: 'Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers.' The passage also includes a hadith reference about a father marrying his minor son, which is here used to show the father's exclusive authority, not the minor's.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): Legal authority to contract a marriage on behalf of another, specifically for minors or those without capacity.
كافر (kafir): A non-Muslim who cannot have any authority over a Muslim, as derived from the Quranic verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following cannot be a marriage guardian according to this passage?
A) A paternal uncle who is a minor.
B) A grandfather who is non-Muslim.
C) A brother who is a slave.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school unequivocally disqualifies four categories from marriage guardianship: slaves, minors, insane persons, and non-Muslims, with the Quranic proof for the latter.

Abu Hanifa's View on Non-Asabah Guardians
Ruling with proof for non-asabah guardianship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that non-asabah relatives may act as marriage guardians and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Guardianship in marriage is based on maslahah, not inheritance; hence non-asabah may act when no asabah exist.

This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's position that when no asabah (agnatic) guardian is available, non-asabah relatives such as the mother, sister, or maternal aunt may perform the marriage. This ruling is supported by prophetic practice and the principle of maslahah. However, Imam Muhammad disagrees, tying guardianship to inheritance rights. We will examine the evidence, reasoning, and which view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
What exactly does Abu Hanifa permit? Under what condition? Note that the ruling applies only when no asabah guardian exists.
The condition is crucial: non-asabah act only in the absence of asabah.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The passage cites two proofs: the action of Aisha (ra) marrying a relative, and Ibn Umar's marriage performed by his maternal uncle. Identify these as ahad hadith and note the Prophet's tacit approval.
These are not explicit commands but practices implying permissibility.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How do these proofs demonstrate permissibility? The Prophet attended Aisha's arranged marriage without objection, and Ibn Umar's uncle acted without being an asabah. This indicates the ruling is based on affection and maslahah.
The absence of prohibition is considered approval in such contexts.
4
Contrast with Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad restricts guardianship to asabah, arguing by qiyas on inheritance: those who inherit should also have the right to give in marriage. Identify his reasoning.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both are from the school.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: if only a mother is available, Abu Hanifa allows her to marry her daughter; Imam Muhammad requires a qadi. The commentary indicates Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi.
Tarjih is based on stronger evidence and maslahah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۷۶۸ (۴۳) وقال ابو حنيفة رحمه الله يجوز لغير العصبات من الاقارب التزويج مثل الاخت والام والخالة [۹] (1) يه ولایت مصلحت کے لئے ہے۔ اور رشتہ دار چاہے دور کے ہوں اس میں شفقت ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے مصلحت کا تقاضا ہے کہ ان کو شادی کرانے کا حق دیا جائے (۲) اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے اپنے رشتہ دار کی شادی کرائی حالانکہ وہ عصبات والی ولیہ نہیں تھیں ۔ عن ابن عباس قال انكحت عائشة ذات قرابة لها من الانصار فجاء رسول الله فقال اهديتم الفتاة؟ قالوا نعم (ب) (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الغناء والدف ص ۲۷۳ نمبر ۱۹۰۰ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے اپنے رشتہ دار کی شادی کرائی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذوی الارحام عورت ہو تو بھی عصبات نہ ہوتے وقت شادی کراتی ہے۔ قال ابن عمر فزوجنيها خالي قدامة وهو عمها ولم يشاورها (سنن ابن ماجه شریف، باب نکاح الصغار یز و جھن غیر الآباء ص ۲۶۹ نمبر ۱۸۷۸) اس اثر میں قدامہ ماموں نے شادی کرائی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ غیر عصبات شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ فائده امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ عصبات ہی شادی کر سکتے ہیں دوسرے نہیں۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ عصبات کو وراثت میں حق ہے تو ولایت میں بھی حق ہوگا۔
Abu Hanifa said: It is permissible for non-asabah relatives to perform marriage, such as the sister, mother, and aunt. ... (then Urdu commentary and proofs)
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage records the position of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding who can act as a marriage guardian when no asabah (agnatic relatives) are available. The Arabic text states that non-asabah relatives like the sister (ukht), mother (umm), and maternal aunt (khalah) may perform the marriage. The commentary provides the rationale: guardianship is based on maslahah (public good), and relatives, even distant ones, have affection. It cites two proofs: (1) Aisha (ra) married a relative of hers from the Ansar, and the Prophet (saw) attended the wedding, implying approval. (2) Ibn Umar reported that his maternal uncle Qudamah married him to a woman without consulting him, indicating that a non-asabah uncle can act. The passage also notes that Imam Muhammad holds a different view: only asabah have guardianship because inheritance rights are tied to guardianship.

Key Terms
عصبات (asabah): Agnatic relatives (male line) who inherit as residuaries, including father, grandfather, brothers, uncles, etc.
ذوی الارحام (dhawi al-arham): Uterine relatives (non-agnatic), such as mother, sister, maternal aunt, who do not inherit as asabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Consensus (ijma) of the Sahaba on the issue.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa allows non-asabah relatives to act as marriage guardians when no asabah exist, based on maslahah and prophetic practice; this is the mufta bihi view despite Imam Muhammad's contrary qiyas.

The Mawla's Right to Marry His Freed Slave Woman
Ruling on the mawla's marriage guardianship over a freed woman without a guardian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and explain the legal basis for the mawla's marriage guardianship over his freed slave woman.

Core Idea
The manumitting master (mawla) is the asabah of his freed slave, giving him marriage guardianship when no blood guardian exists.

This lesson clarifies a specific scenario: a freed slave woman who has no blood guardian (wali). Who may contract her marriage? The Hanafi school rules that her manumitting master (mawla) has this right. The reasoning is grounded in the principle of asabah: the mawla is the residuary heir of the freed slave and thus also holds guardianship. Understanding this demonstrates how the school extends wilayah (guardianship) through legal relationships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mawla contracting marriage for his freed woman. The ruling is that the marriage is valid (jā'iz).
2
Locate the condition
The condition is that the woman has no guardian (wali) of her own.
3
Trace the legal basis
The mawla is considered an asabah (residuary heir) of the freed slave, based on the principle that the mawla inherits from the freed slave.
4
Apply the principle
Since asabah includes guardianship, the mawla has the right to marry her.

Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This short passage deals with a specific case: a freed slave woman who has no guardian at all. The Arabic ruling states that her manumitting master (mawla) may contract her marriage, and it is valid. The commentary explains the reasoning: the mawla is considered an asabah (residuary heir) of the freed slave, because in the absence of blood relatives, the mawla inherits from the freed slave. Since he is an asabah, he also has guardianship (wilayah) in marriage. This is consistent with the principle that guardianship follows inheritance priority.

Key Terms
مولی (mawla): The master who emancipates a slave; in the absence of asabah, he becomes the guardian and residuary heir.
عصبة (asabah): Residuary heir who inherits after prescribed shares; also holds guardianship in marriage.

Marriage Guardianship by Non-Aṣaba Relatives
Explaining Abu Hanifa's ruling on non-aṣaba guardians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on marriage guardianship by non-aṣaba relatives, identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
When no aṣaba guardian exists, non-aṣaba relatives may perform marriage – guardianship is based on benefit, not inheritance.

This passage presents Abu Hanifa's ruling that non-aṣaba relatives (like sister, mother, maternal aunt) can validly contract a marriage when no aṣaba guardian is available. The commentary defends this against objections, citing Quranic and prophetic evidence, and contrasts it with Imam Muhammad's view. Understanding this ruling clarifies who may act as guardian in the absence of close agnates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Abu Hanifa allows non-aṣaba relatives (sister, mother, maternal aunt) to perform marriage when no aṣaba exists. Note the scope: they are not primary guardians but substitutes.
This is a permissive ruling, not obligatory.
2
Understand the objection and response
The objection: those without self-guardianship (slave, child, insane, disbeliever) cannot have guardianship over others. The response distinguishes between incapacity and religious prohibition. The Quranic verse (4:141) proves disbelievers cannot have authority.
The verse is used to exclude disbelievers specifically.
3
Examine the positive evidence
Two narrations: Aisha (RA) married a relative from the Ansar, and Qudama (maternal uncle) married Ibn Umar. These show practice of non-aṣaba guardians. Also maṣlaḥa reasoning: relatives have affection and can act for benefit.
The hadith are from Ibn Majah.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad restricts guardianship to aṣaba only, using qiyās on inheritance rights. Abu Hanifa counters that guardianship is based on maṣlaḥa, not inheritance, and the narrations override the analogy.
The relied-upon fatwa is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
