Father's Authority in Mahr for Minor Children
Ruling on father's discretion in mahr for minor children and limit of excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on a father's authority to adjust mahr for minor children and distinguish Abu Hanifa's view of unlimited maṣlaḥa from the Sahibayn's limit of a minor excess.

Core Idea
A father may adjust mahr for a minor child's marriage based on maṣlaḥa, but the Sahibayn limit the deviation to a trivial amount.

This passage addresses a key question in Hanafi nikah: can a father (or grandfather) reduce his daughter's mahr or increase his son's mahr when marrying them off as minors? The author explains that due to their deep affection and wisdom, they have a special authority, but there is an internal dispute over how far they can go. You will learn the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and the role of maṣlaḥa in justifying minor harms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is the father (or grandfather) marrying off his minor child with a deviation from mahr al-mithl. The ruling is that the marriage is valid (sahih), but there may be liability if the deviation is excessive.
The act is valid ab initio, but the father may owe compensation if he exceeds limits according to some views.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Abu Hanifa holds that the father has unlimited discretion to reduce the daughter's mahr or increase the son's mahr as long as there is an overall maṣlaḥa (benefit). The proof is the hadith of Aisha's marriage at age six, which shows that a greater benefit can outweigh a minor loss in mahr.
The hadith is considered zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala but supports the principle of overriding a lesser maṣlaḥa for a greater one.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and limit
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) restrict the father's authority: only a minor deviation (up to three dirhams or a similar trivial amount) is permissible. Beyond that, the marriage is still valid, but the father may be liable for the deficiency.
The Sahibayn argue that a large deviation harms the child's interest and cannot be justified by maṣlaḥa.
4
Understand the basis: maṣlaḥa and the hadith
Both views rely on the concept of maṣlaḥa. Abu Hanifa sees maṣlaḥa broadly; the Sahibayn define it narrowly by capping the loss. The hadith of Aisha demonstrates that the Prophet married a minor for a great maṣlaḥa (being the Prophet's wife), even though mahr considerations were secondary.
The hadith is used as a precedent for overriding a minor harm for a greater benefit.
5
Note who holds this authority
Only the father and grandfather have this combination of affection and wisdom. Other relatives (brother, mother) lack one or the other, so they cannot deviate from mahr al-mithl without the child's consent (or the child's guardian's permission).
This highlights the unique position of the father and grandfather in Hanafi marriage law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۷۷۷) (۵۲) اگر باپ نے اپنی چھوٹی بیٹی کی شادی کرائی اور مہر مشکل سے کم رکھا۔ یا چھوٹے بیٹے کی شادی کرائی اور اس کی بیوی کی مہر میں زیادہ کیا تو یہ دونوں پر جائز ہے۔ اور نہیں جائز ہے باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کے لئے ۔ باپ اور دادا میں شفقت کا ملہ ہے اور عقل بھی ہے۔ اس لئے وہ اگر بیٹے یا بیٹی کے ساتھ مہر کے معاملے میں کچھ زیادتی کرے تو یہ قابل برداشت ہے۔ مثلا چھوٹی بیٹی کی شادی کی اور مہر مثل سے کم مہر رکھا یا چھوٹے بیٹے کی شادی کی اور اس کی بیوی کا جومہ مثل بنتا ہے اس سے زیادہ رکھا تو ان کے لئے یہ جائز ہے اور نکاح ہو جائے گا۔
مہر کے بارے میں اگر چہ زیادتی کی ہے لیکن اس کے علاوہ اور مصالح ہیں جن کی وجہ سے انہوں نے یہ زیادتی برداشت کی ہوگی اس لئے مہر کی کمی بیشی قابل قبول ہوگی (۲) عن عائشة ان النبی الا الله تزوجها وهى بنت ست سنين وادخلت عليه وهي بنت تسع و مكشت عنده تسعا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب اتکاح الرجل ولده الصغارص اے کے نمبر ۵۱۳۳) اس حدیث میں چھوٹی لڑکی کی شادی تریپن سال کے آدمی سے کرائی تاہم اس لئے جائز ہو گیا کہ حضور کے ساتھ شادی تھی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بڑی مصلحت کی خاطر چھوٹی مصلحت کو نظر انداز کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ تین فاحش تک مہر میں کمی کرنا یا زیادتی کرنا قابل قبول ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ مصلحت کے خلاف ہے اس لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔
باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں یا تو شفقت کا ملہ نہیں ہے جیسے چا وغیرہ یاعقل کام نہیں ہے جیسے ماں ۔ اس لئے ان لوگوں نے کی زیادتی کے ساتھ شادی کرائی تو قابل قبول نہیں ہوگا۔
[1777] (52) If a father marries off his minor daughter and reduces from her mahr al-mithl, or marries off his minor son and increases his wife's mahr beyond the mahr al-mithl, then that is permissible for both. But it is not permissible for anyone other than the father and grandfather. The father and grandfather have an abundance of affection and wisdom. Therefore, if they cause some excess in the matter of mahr regarding the son or daughter, it is tolerable. For example, marrying off the minor daughter with less than mahr al-mithl, or marrying off the minor son and increasing the mahr of his wife beyond what is mahr al-mithl, then for them it is permissible and the marriage is valid. Even though there is excess in mahr, but there are other maṣāliḥ (benefits) due to which they may have tolerated this excess; therefore, the decrease or increase of mahr is acceptable. (2) From Aisha that the Prophet married her when she was six years old and consummated when she was nine, and she remained with him nine years. (alif) (Bukhari, chapter on a man marrying off his minor children, no. 5133). In this hadith, a minor girl was married to a fifty-three-year-old man, but it became permissible because it was the Prophet's marriage. From this it is understood that for a greater maṣlaḥa, a lesser maṣlaḥa can be overlooked. The Sahibayn say that up to three vile things (i.e., a minor excess) in increase or decrease of mahr is acceptable; beyond that, it is contrary to maṣlaḥa, so not permissible. For other than father and grandfather, either there is no abundance of affection (like a brother) or no wisdom (like a mother), so if they contract a marriage with excess (in mahr), it is not acceptable.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage discusses the father's (and grandfather's) authority to deviate from mahr al-mithl when marrying off minor children. The author argues that due to their affection and wisdom, they may reduce the daughter's mahr or increase the son's mahr if there is some overall benefit (e.g., a good match). The hadith of Aisha's marriage at a young age to the Prophet is cited as precedent that greater maṣlaḥa can outweigh a minor loss (here, possible deficiency in mahr). The Sahibayn limit this discretion: only a minor excess (three dirhams or similar) is allowed; beyond that it is not permissible because it harms the child's interest. The text also clarifies that only father and grandfather have this authority; others (e.g., brother, mother) do not have the same combination of affection and wisdom.

Key Terms
مصلحت (maṣlaḥah): Benefit or interest that justifies a legal ruling, even if it involves a minor harm.
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard mahr for a woman of similar status in her community; used as a baseline when mahr is not specified or is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the maximum deviation from mahr al-mithl that a father may make for his minor child?
A) No deviation at all.
B) Up to three dirhams (or a minor amount).
C) Up to ten dirhams.
D) Unlimited, as long as there is maṣlaḥa.

Key Takeaway
A father may adjust mahr for his minor child's marriage based on maṣlaḥa, but the Sahibayn require the deviation to be minor; otherwise the father may face liability.

8 min
Father's Authority to Set Mahr for Minor Children
Hanafi ruling on father's mahr adjustment with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on father's authority to adjust mahr for minors, identify the exclusive guardians, and explain the Sahibayn's threefold restriction.

Core Idea
Only father and grandfather can reduce or increase mahr for minors due to their compassion and wisdom.

This lesson examines a unique Hanafi rule: a father or paternal grandfather may marry off his minor children and set a mahr below or above the proper mahr (mahr al-mithl). This discretion is not granted to any other guardian. The reasoning combines textual proof from the Prophet's marriage to Aisha with an understanding of guardianship. We also explore a key intra-Hanafi debate: the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) restrict the deviation to three times the proper mahr, while the earlier text is silent on a limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
State the hukm: the father or grandfather may reduce or increase the mahr for his minor child; the marriage is valid. Note that this permission is exclusive to the father and grandfather.
The text explicitly excludes all other guardians (brother, mother, uncle, etc.).
2
Examine the Proof (Dalil)
The hadith of Aisha (Bukhari no. 5133) is cited: the Prophet married her at age six. The commentary argues that this shows a greater benefit (marriage with the Prophet) can override a lesser one (standard mahr), thus permitting deviation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but the Hanafi school accepts it for establishing rulings.
3
Analyze the Reasoning (Ta'lil)
Only the father and grandfather combine both compassion (shafaqah) and sound judgment (aql). Other guardians lack one or both qualities: e.g., the mother has compassion but not necessarily judgment; the brother may have judgment but not the same compassion.
This explains why the ruling is restricted to these two.
4
Explore the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
The Sahibayn qualify the ruling: the deviation must not exceed three times the proper mahr. Beyond that, it is against the child's interest and impermissible. The text does not explicitly limit, but the commentary leans toward this restriction.
The practical difference: under Sahibayn, a father who sets mahr ten times the proper mahr would be liable, but the marriage remains valid.

واذا زوج الاب ابنته الصغيرة ونقص من مهر مثلها او ابنه الصغير وزاد فى مهر امرأته جاز ذلك عليهما ولا يجوز ذلك لغير الاب والجد [١٧٧٧] (٥٢) اگر باپ نے اپنی چھوٹی بیٹی کی شادی کرائی اور مہر مثل سے کم رکھا۔ یا چھوٹے بیٹے کی شادی کرائی اور اس کی بیوی کی مہر میں زیادہ کیا تو یہ دونوں پر جائز ہے۔ اور نہیں جائز ہے باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ کے لئے ۔ باپ اور دادا میں شفقت کا ملہ ہے اور عقل بھی ہے۔ اس لئے وہ اگر بیٹے یا بیٹی کے ساتھ مہر کے معاملے میں کچھ زیادتی کرے تو یہ قابل برداشت ہے۔ مثلا چھوٹی بیٹی کی شادی کی اور مہر مثل سے کم مہر رکھا یا چھوٹے بیٹے کی شادی کی اور اس کی بیوی کا جومہ مثل بنتا ہے اس سے زیادہ رکھا تو ان کے لئے یہ جائز ہے اور نکاح ہو جائے گا۔ مہر کے بارے میں اگر چہ زیادتی کی ہے لیکن اس کے علاوہ اور مصالح ہیں جن کی وجہ سے انہوں نے یہ زیادتی برداشت کی ہوگی اس لئے مہر کی کمی بیشی قابل قبول ہوگی (٢) عن عائشة ان النبی ﷺ تزوجها وهى بنت ست سنين وادخلت عليه وهي بنت تسع و مكشت عنده تسعا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب اتکاح الرجل ولده الصغارص اے کے نمبر ٥١٣٣) اس حدیث میں چھوٹی لڑکی کی شادی تریپن سال کے آدمی سے کرائی تاہم اس لئے جائز ہو گیا کہ حضور کے ساتھ شادی تھی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بڑی مصلحت کی خاطر چھوٹی مصلحت کو نظر انداز کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ تین فاحش تک مہر میں کمی کرنا یا زیادتی کرنا قابل قبول ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ مصلحت کے خلاف ہے اس لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ باپ اور دادا کے علاوہ میں یا تو شفقت کا ملہ نہیں ہے جیسے چا وغیرہ یاعقل کام نہیں ہے جیسے ماں ۔ اس لئے ان لوگوں نے کی زیادتی کے ساتھ شادی کرائی تو قابل قبول نہیں ہوگا۔
And if the father marries his minor daughter and reduces from her proper mahr, or (marries) his minor son and increases in the mahr of his wife, that is permissible upon them both, and that is not permissible for other than the father and the grandfather. [1777] (52) If the father arranged the marriage of his minor daughter and set a mahr less than the proper mahr, or arranged the marriage of his minor son and increased the mahr of his wife, this is permissible for both. And it is not permissible for other than the father and grandfather. The father and grandfather possess the quality of compassion and wisdom. Therefore, if they make some excess in the matter of mahr for their son or daughter, it is tolerable. For example, he married his minor daughter and set a mahr less than the proper mahr, or married his minor son and set more than the proper mahr for his wife, then this is permissible for them and the marriage will be valid. Even if there is excess in the mahr, there are other considerations for which they may have tolerated this excess, so the reduction or increase in mahr is acceptable. (2) From Aisha that the Prophet ﷺ married her when she was six years old, and she was entered to him when she was nine, and she remained with him for nine years. (a) (Bukhari, Chapter on a man marrying his minor children, hadith no. 5133) In this hadith, a minor girl's marriage was arranged with a fifty-three-year-old man, but it became valid because it was marriage with the Prophet. This shows that for a greater benefit, a lesser benefit can be overlooked. The Sahibayn say that reducing or increasing the mahr up to three times [the proper mahr] is acceptable. More than that is against benefit, so it is not permissible. For other than father and grandfather, either they lack the quality of compassion (like a brother) or they lack wisdom (like a mother). Therefore, if these people arrange a marriage with excess, it will not be acceptable.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling and its proof. The ruling: a father or grandfather may marry off his minor children and may set a mahr that either undercuts or exceeds the proper mahr (mahr al-mithl). This is exclusive to the father and paternal grandfather; no other guardian (e.g., brother, mother, uncle) can do so. The reasoning: only the father and grandfather combine both compassion and sound judgment, so their discretion in such matters is trusted. The passage provides a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ married Aisha at a young age, showing that benefits can override the standard mahr consideration. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) qualify this: the deviation must not exceed three times the proper mahr; beyond that, it is against the child's benefit.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper mahr; the mahr that a woman of similar status would receive in her locality and family.
اب (ab): Father; the only guardian besides the paternal grandfather who can adjust mahr for minors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who among the following can validly reduce the mahr of a minor daughter below the proper mahr according to the Hanafi school?
A) The mother
B) The paternal grandfather
C) The brother
D) The uncle

Key Takeaway
Father and grandfather alone may adjust mahr for minors; the Sahibayn's threefold limit is the relied-upon position in practice.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Validity of Marriage with or without Specified Mahr
Hanafi ruling that marriage is valid whether mahr is specified or not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of marriage when mahr is not specified and explain the proof from Quran 4:24.

Core Idea
Marriage is valid without specifying mahr – mahr is obligatory but not a condition.

Many assume that a marriage contract requires the mahr to be named. In the Hanafi school, mahr is an obligation but its specification is not a condition for validity. This lesson examines the ruling and its scriptural basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: marriage is valid whether mahr is specified or not.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic evidence: Surah an-Nisa 4:24, which commands seeking with wealth.
3
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the phrase 'tabtaghu bi-amwalikum' indicates obligation of mahr but not its specification at contract.
4
Distinguish obligation from condition
Recognize that mahr is fard (obligatory) but not a shart (condition) for validity.
5
Determine the consequence
If no mahr is specified, mahr al-mithl (proper mahr) becomes due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصح النكاح اذا سمى فيه مهرا ويصح النكاح ان لم يسم فيه مهرا [١٧٧٨] (٥٣) ويصح النكاح اذا سمى فيه مهرا نکاح صحیح ہے جبکہ متعین کرے اس میں مہر اور صحیح ہے نکاح اگر چہ متعین نہیں کیا ہو اس میں مہر۔ نکاح کرتے وقت مہر کا نام لے یا نہ لے دونوں صورتوں میں نکاح درست ہے۔ مہر تو نص قطعی اور آیت کی وجہ سے فرض ہے۔ اس لئے اس کا نام نہ بھی لے تب بھی نکاح درست ہو جائے گا۔ اور مہر مثل لازم ہو جائے گا (٢) آیت میں فرض ہونے کی دلیل موجود ہے۔ واحل لکم ماوراء ذلكم ان تبتغوا باموالكم محصنين غير مسافحين (الف) ( آیت ٢٤ سورة النساء ٤) اس آیت میں تبتغوا باموالکم سے مہر فرض ہونے کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ اس لئے مہر متعین کئے بغیر بھی شادی ہو جائے گی۔ اور آیت کی وجہ سے خود بخود مہر لازم ہو جائے گا۔
And the marriage is valid if mahr is specified in it, and the marriage is valid if mahr is not specified in it. [1778] (53) And the marriage is valid if mahr is specified in it. Marriage is valid when mahr is specified in it, and marriage is valid even if mahr is not specified in it. At the time of marriage, whether one mentions the mahr or not, both cases the marriage is correct. Mahr is obligatory by definitive text and verse. Therefore, even if one does not mention it, the marriage will still be valid, and the proper mahr (mahr al-mithl) becomes obligatory. (2) The evidence for obligation is present in the verse: 'And lawful to you are those beyond [these] that you seek with your wealth, being chaste, not fornicators' (Quran 4:24). In this verse, 'you seek with your wealth' indicates the obligation of mahr. Therefore, the marriage will take place even without specifying the mahr, and due to the verse, the mahr will automatically become obligatory.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling followed by proof. The ruling states that marriage is valid whether or not a specific mahr is mentioned at the time of contract. The commentator explains that mahr is obligatory by a definitive text (a clear Quranic verse), but specifying it is not a condition for the validity of the marriage. If no mahr is specified, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the proper mahr). The proof is from Quran 4:24, where 'seeking with wealth' implies that mahr is a requirement, but the verse does not condition it on specification. This is a fundamental Hanafi principle distinguishing between obligation and condition.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper mahr for a woman of similar status; becomes obligatory when no mahr is specified.
فرض (fard): Obligatory; mahr is fard in the sense that it must be paid, but it is not a pillar (rukn) of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a couple marries without specifying any mahr, what is the status of the marriage according to the Hanafi school?
A) The marriage is invalid (batil)
B) The marriage is valid but mahr is not obligatory
C) The marriage is valid and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl
D) The marriage is valid only if they later agree on a mahr

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, marriage is valid whether mahr is specified or not; if not specified, mahr al-mithl is obligatory.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Minimum Mahr: The Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Debate
Full inter-madhhab dispute on minimum mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi minimum mahr (ten dirhams), explain the proofs, and apply the ruling in contrast to the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Hanafi: mahr minimum is ten dirhams; other schools accept less.

What happens if a husband and wife agree to a mahr of only five dirhams? According to the Hanafi school, the wife is still entitled to ten dirhams. But the Shafi'i and Maliki schools accept lesser amounts. This lesson explores the evidence behind the Hanafi position and the points of dispute with other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Identify the core ruling: minimum mahr is ten dirhams. Note the hadith from Jabir and the Quranic inference (significant wealth) used as evidence.
2
Present the Shafi'i view and their proof
Understand that the Shafi'i school does not set a minimum; they rely on the hadith of the iron ring, which permitted a minimal mahr.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi response argues that the iron ring hadith is specific to that individual and does not establish a general rule; the hadith from Jabir sets a clear minimum.
4
Present the Maliki view and their proof
The Maliki school requires a minimum of a quarter dinar. Their proof includes the hadith of the two sandals and an analogy from the theft hadith (hand cut for quarter dinar).
5
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Maliki proof and determine thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy from theft because mahr is a contractual right, not a penal value. The practical difference: under Hanafi, a mahr less than ten dirhams must be supplemented; under Maliki, a mahr less than quarter dinar is invalid; under Shafi'i, any amount is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١٧٧٩] (٥٤) واقل المهر عشرة دراهم فان سمى اور کم سے کم مہر دس درہم ہے۔ پس اگر متعین کیا دس درہم سے کم تو اس کے لئے دس درہم ہیں ۔ نکاح میں کم سے کم مہر دس درہم ہے۔ اور اگر اس سے کم مہر رکھا پھر بھی عورت کو دس درہم ملیں گے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ مہر دس درہم سے کم نہ ہو ۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لا صداق دون عشرة در اهم (الف) (دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح، ج ثالث ص ۷۳ انمبر ۳۵۶۰ سفن للبیہقی ، باب ما یجوزان یکون مہراج سابع ص ۳۹۲ نمبر ۱۴۳۸۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مہر دس درہم سے کم نہ ہو (٢) او پر آیت میں تھا کہ تبتغوا باموالکم جس سے اندازہ ہوتا ہے کہ کوئی اہم مال ہو۔ اور دس درہم سے کم اہم مال نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بضعہ کی قیمت اہم مال ہونا چاہئے اور وہ دس درہم ہے۔ نان امام شافعی کے نزدیک جتنے مال پر میاں بیوی متفق ہو جائیں وہ مال لازم ہو گا چاہے لو ہے کی انگوٹھی ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔ ان کی دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں آپ نے فرمایا کہ جاؤ لوہے کی انگوٹھی ہی تلاش کر کے لاؤ۔ سـمـعـت سهل بن سعد الساعدى يـقــول انـي لـفـي القوم عند رسول الله الله اذ قامت امرأة ... قال الله الله اذهب فاطلب ولو خاتما من حديد (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب التزويج على القرآن و بغیر صداق ص ۷۴ ۷ نمبر ۵۱۴۹ر مسلم شریف ، باب الصداق و جواز کو نہ تعلیم قرآن ص ۴۵۷ نمبر ۱۴۲۵) اس حدیث میں لوہے کی انگوٹھی تلاش کرنے کے لئے کہا جو بہت کم قیمت ہوتی ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کم قیمت کی چیز بھی مہر بن سکتی ہے۔ اور امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ چوتھائی دینار سے کم نہ ہو۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ سمعت عبد الله بن عامر بن ربيعة عن ابيه ان امرأة من بني فزارة تزوجت على نعلين فقال رسول الله ارضيت من نفسک و مالک بنعلين قالت نعم قال فاجازه ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی مهور النسا ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۱۱۳) اس حدیث میں دو جوتے پر شادی کی ہے جو تقریبا چوتھائی دینار کا ہوتا ہے (٢) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت قال النبي لا تقطع اليد في ربع دينار فصاعدا ( بخاری شریف، باب قول الله تعالى والسارق والسارقة فاقطعوا اید معما وفي كم يقطع ص ۱۰۰۳ نمبر ۶۷۸۹) اس حدیث میں چوتھائی دینار کے بدلے چور کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک عضو کی کم سے کم قیمت چوتھائی دینار ہے۔ اور مہر بھی ایک عضو کی قیمت ہے اس لئے وہ بھی چوتھائی دینار سے کم نہیں ہونا چاہئے۔ گنجائش ہو تو مہر فاطمی مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ آپ کی ازواج مطہرات کا مہر بھی مہر فاطمی یعنی پانچ سو درہم تھا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ سالت عائشة زوج النبي كم كان صداق رسول الله ؟ قالت كان صداقه لازواجه ثنتى وشرة اوقية و نشاء قالت اتدرى ما النش؟ قال قلت لا ، قالت نصف اوقية فتلك خمس مائة درهم، فهذا صداق رسول الله لا زواجه(مسلم شریف، باب حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے فرمایا کہ مہر دس درہم سے کم نہیں ہے (ب) سہل بن سعد فرماتے ہیں کہ میں کچھ لوگوں کے ساتھ آپ کی خدمت میں تھا کہ ایک عورت کھڑی ہوئی ۔ آپ نے فرمایا جاؤ! پس ایک انگوٹھی ہی تلاش کر کے لاؤ چاہے لوہے کی ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔
[1779] (54) And the minimum mahr is ten dirhams, so if he specifies less than ten dirhams, then he owes ten dirhams. The minimum mahr in marriage is ten dirhams. If he sets a mahr less than that, the woman will still receive ten dirhams. There is a hadith that mahr should not be less than ten dirhams. From Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'There is no dower less than ten dirhams' (a) (Darqutni, Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 3 p.73 no. 3560; and al-Bayhaqi, Bab ma Yajuz an yakuna mahr... vol. 7 p.392 no. 14384). From this hadith it is known that mahr should not be less than ten dirhams. (2) And the earlier verse stated: 'you seek with your wealth', indicating that there should be some significant wealth. Less than ten dirhams is not significant wealth. Therefore, the price for the vulva must be significant wealth, and that is ten dirhams. According to Imam Shafi'i, whatever amount the spouses agree upon, that amount becomes binding, even if it is an iron ring. Their evidence is the hadith in which the Prophet said: 'Go and seek, even if it is an iron ring.' (b) (Bukhari, Bab al-Tazwij ala al-Qur'an wa bighayr Sadaq... p.747 no. 5149; Muslim, Bab al-Sadaq wa Jawaz... p.457 no. 1425). In this hadith, he was told to seek an iron ring, which is very low in value. This shows that a low-value item can also be mahr. Imam Malik says that it should not be less than a quarter dinar. Their evidence is this hadith: I heard Abdullah ibn Amir ibn Rabi'a from his father that a woman from Banu Fazara married for two sandals, and the Messenger of Allah said: 'Are you pleased with yourself and your wealth for two sandals?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'I permit it.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi Mahr al-Nisa, p.211 no. 113). In this hadith, the marriage was for two sandals, which is approximately a quarter dinar. (2) Another hadith: From Aisha who said the Prophet said: 'The hand is not cut off for less than a quarter dinar.' (Bukhari, Bab Qawl Allah... p.1003 no. 6789). In this hadith, the thief's hand is cut off for a quarter dinar. From this it is known that the minimum value of a body part is a quarter dinar. And mahr is also the price for a body part, so it should not be less than a quarter dinar. If possible, the Fatimi mahr is recommended, because the mahr of the pure wives of the Prophet was the Fatimi mahr, i.e., five hundred dirhams. In a hadith: I asked Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, how much was the dower of the Messenger of Allah? She said: His dower for his wives was twelve uqiyas and a nashsh. She said: Do you know what nashsh is? He said: I said no. She said: Half an uqiya, so that is five hundred dirhams. This is the dower of the Messenger of Allah for his wives. (Muslim, Bab... ) Footnote (a): The Prophet said that mahr is not less than ten dirhams. (b): Sahl ibn Sa'd said: I was among some people with the Prophet when a woman stood up... The Prophet said: Go! So seek a ring even if it is an iron one.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with inter-madhhab dispute. It first states the Hanafi position: minimum mahr is ten dirhams (approximately 30 grams of silver). If less is specified, the wife is entitled to ten dirhams. The proof is a hadith reported by Jabir that no dower is less than ten dirhams [this hadith is weak in some views but accepted by Hanafis]. Additionally, from Quran 4:24, the phrase 'seeking with wealth' implies something of value, and less than ten dirhams is not considered valuable wealth. Then the passage presents the Shafi'i view: any amount agreed upon is valid, even an iron ring, citing the hadith of the iron ring. The Hanafi response (implicit) is that the iron ring hadith is not absolute; it was for a specific case and does not fix a minimum. Next is the Maliki view: minimum is a quarter dinar (approx. 1.0625 grams of gold), using the hadith of the sandals and the analogy from theft (hand is cut for quarter dinar). The Hanafi response is that the analogy is weak because mahr is not a penal value. The passage ends with the recommendation of Fatimi mahr (500 dirhams) as a sunnah, not a minimum.

Key Terms
درهم (dirham): A silver coin; ten dirhams is approximately 29.75 grams of silver, the minimum mahr.
مهر فاطمي (mahr al-Fatimi): The mahr of Fatima (daughter of the Prophet), set at 500 dirhams, recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a husband agrees to a mahr of 5 dirhams?
A) The marriage is invalid
B) The wife receives only 5 dirhams
C) The wife must receive 10 dirhams as minimum mahr
D) The mahr is deferred until divorce

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixes the minimum mahr at ten dirhams, based on a specific hadith and the Quranic requirement of significant wealth.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
12 min
Minimum Mahr and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute on minimum mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi minimum mahr, identify the primary dalil, and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Core Idea
The Hanafi minimum mahr is ten dirhams — a hadith establishes this as the threshold for significant wealth.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the minimum mahr (dower) in marriage. The source presents the core ruling, its evidence from the hadith 'La sadaqa duna 'asharati darahim,' and the Quranic implication that mahr must be significant wealth. It then addresses the objections of Imam Shafi'i (who allows any amount) and Imam Malik (who sets a quarter dinar minimum). By the end, you will understand why the Hanafi school insists on ten dirhams and how this impacts real marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on minimum mahr
Read the passage and identify the explicit ruling: the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. If less is specified, the woman still receives ten.
This is a wajib (obligatory) ruling.
2
Identify the primary dalil
Locate the hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah ('La sadaqa duna 'asharati darahim') and the Quranic phrase 'tabtaghu bi-amwalikum' (4:24). Understand how the Hanafi school uses them.
The hadith is considered mutawatir in meaning by Hanafis.
3
Examine the Shafi'i objection and its dalil
Read the Shafi'i position: no minimum mahr; any agreed amount suffices, even an iron ring. Their evidence is the hadith of the iron ring.
4
Examine the Maliki objection and its dalil
Read the Maliki position: minimum is a quarter dinar. Their evidence: the hadith of marriage for two sandals and the hadith on cutting the hand for a quarter dinar.
5
Determine the Hanafi response and practical difference
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith of the iron ring shows permissibility of low value in principle, but the minimum is set by other proofs. For Malikis, the vulva's value is analogized to the hand, but Hanafis reject the analogy because the hadith of ten dirhams specifies the amount.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): In Shafi'i, a mahr of a date is valid; in Hanafi, the woman always gets at least ten dirhams.

زوج النبي كم كان صداق رسول الله ؟ قالت كان صداقه لازواجه ثنتى وشرة اوقية و نشاء قالت اتدرى ما النش؟ قال قلت لا ، قالت نصف اوقية فتلك خمس مائة درهم، فهذا صداق رسول الله لا زواجه(مسلم شریف، باب حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے فرمایا کہ مہر دس درہم سے کم نہیں ہے (ب) سہل بن سعد فرماتے ہیں کہ میں کچھ لوگوں کے ساتھ آپ کی خدمت میں تھا کہ ایک عورت کھڑی ہوئی ۔ آپ نے فرمایا جاؤ! پس ایک انگوٹھی ہی تلاش کر کے لاؤ چاہے لوہے کی ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔
Marriage is valid even if no mahr is specified in it. The minimum mahr is ten dirhams. So if one specifies less than ten dirhams, she gets ten dirhams. The minimum mahr in marriage is ten dirhams. And if a mahr less than that is set, the woman still gets ten dirhams. There is a hadith: the mahr should not be less than ten dirhams: from Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'No dower less than ten dirhams.' (al-F) (Dar Qutni, Book of Nikah, vol 3 p 73 no 3560, and al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what may be a mahr, vol 7 p 392 no 14384) From this hadith it is known that the mahr is not less than ten dirhams. And earlier in the verse there was 'that you seek with your wealth' (4:24) which indicates that it should be significant wealth. And less than ten dirhams is not significant wealth. Therefore the price of the vulva should be significant wealth, and that is ten dirhams. According to Imam Shafi'i, whatever wealth the spouses agree upon becomes binding, even if it is an iron ring. Their proof is the hadith where the Prophet said: 'Go and find even an iron ring.' (b) (Bukhari, chapter on marriage on the Quran and without mahr p 747 no 5149; Muslim, chapter on dower and permissibility of teaching Quran p 457 no 1425) In this hadith, he was told to look for an iron ring, which is of very low value. From this it is known that a low-value item can be a mahr. Imam Malik says it should not be less than a quarter dinar. His proof is this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Amir ibn Rabi'a from his father that a woman from Bani Fazarah was married for two sandals. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Are you satisfied with yourself and your property for two sandals?' She said yes, so he permitted it. (Tirmidhi, chapter on mahr of women p 211 no 113) In this hadith, marriage was for two sandals, which is approximately a quarter dinar. Another hadith: from Aisha, the Prophet said: 'The hand is not cut off for less than a quarter dinar.' (Bukhari, chapter on the word of Allah 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands' and how much is the minimum for cutting p 1003 no 6789) In this hadith, the thief's hand was cut for a quarter dinar. From this it is known that the minimum value of a limb is a quarter dinar. And mahr is also the price of a limb (the vulva), so it should not be less than a quarter dinar. If there is capacity, the Fatimi mahr is recommended because the mahr of the pure wives of the Prophet was also the Fatimi mahr, i.e., five hundred dirhams. In a hadith: I asked Aisha: 'What was the mahr of the wives of the Prophet?' She said: 'His mahr for his wives was twelve uqiya and a nash.' She said: 'Do you know what a nash is?' I said no. She said: 'Half an uqiya, so that is five hundred dirhams. That was the mahr of the Messenger of Allah for his wives.' (Muslim, chapter on ... ) Footnote: (al-F) The Prophet said that the mahr is not less than ten dirhams. (b) Sahl ibn Sa'd said: I was with some people in the presence of the Prophet when a woman stood up... He said: 'Go! So find a ring even if it is of iron.'
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the minimum mahr. The commentator begins by stating the Hanafi position: marriage is valid even without specifying a mahr (this is based on Quran 4:24 which permits marriage without mentioning a dower). However, if no mahr is specified, the woman is entitled to mahr al-mithl (proper dower). The minimum mahr in Hanafi law is ten dirhams. If someone specifies a mahr less than ten dirhams, the woman still receives ten dirhams, because the contract is valid and the mahr cannot be less than the minimum. The proof is a hadith narrated by Jabir ibn Abdullah: 'No dower less than ten dirhams' (reported by Dar Qutni and Bayhaqi). This hadith establishes the minimum. Additionally, the Quranic phrase 'that you seek with your wealth' (māl) implies that what is given must be considered significant wealth, and less than ten dirhams is not significant in the Hanafi view. The passage then presents the positions of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik. Shafi'i holds that any amount agreed upon, even an iron ring, suffices. His evidence is the hadith where the Prophet told a man to marry even with an iron ring. The Hanafi response is that this hadith indicates permissibility of a small amount, but the minimum of ten dirhams is from other proofs. Imam Malik holds the minimum is a quarter dinar, using the hadith of the woman married for two sandals (approximating a quarter dinar) and the hadith on cutting the hand for a quarter dinar. The Hanafi response is that the mahr is the price of the vulva, which is like a hand, but the vulva's value is determined by the hadith specifying ten dirhams, not analogy to theft. Finally, the commentator mentions that the Fatimi mahr (five hundred dirhams) is recommended for those who can afford it, as it was the mahr of the Prophet's wives. The hadith from Aisha confirms this. Therefore, the Hanafi school firmly establishes ten dirhams as the minimum mahr, with proofs from hadith and reasoning.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife as an obligatory payment upon marriage.
درهم (dirham): A silver coin; in this context, the standard dirham is approximately 2.975 grams of silver, so ten dirhams is about 29.75 grams.
بضع (bud'): The vulva, used metaphorically for the wife's right to sexual intercourse, which is the subject of the mahr contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum mahr according to the Hanafi school?
A) No minimum, any amount agreed upon
B) Ten dirhams
C) Quarter dinar
D) Five hundred dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates a minimum mahr of ten dirhams, based on explicit hadith and the principle that mahr must be significant wealth; differing schools allow lower amounts.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Rulings on Specified Mahr: Full upon Consummation or Death, Half upon Pre-Consummation Divorce
Rulings on specified mahr: binding upon consummation or death, half upon divorce before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specified mahr upon consummation, death, and divorce before consummation, and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Full mahr is due upon consummation or death; half upon divorce before consummation.

This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri presents the core Hanafi rulings on what happens to a specified mahr after marriage. The rulings are straightforward: consummation or death triggers the full mahr, divorce before consummation triggers half. The author supports this with the famous hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq and explains the rationale behind each scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The ruling depends on what happens after marriage: consummation, death of either spouse, or divorce before consummation. Each has a different mahr consequence.
Consummation includes valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) in Hanafi law.
2
State the mahr consequence for each scenario
Full specified mahr is due upon consummation or death of either spouse. Half of the specified mahr is due upon divorce before consummation and before valid seclusion.
If mahr is less than ten dirhams, the default minimum (ten dirhams) applies.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq via Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and Ma'qil ibn Sinan. The Prophet ruled that a woman whose husband died before consummation without specifying a mahr receives the full mahr al-mithl.
This hadith is used by analogy: if unspecified mahr is due in full upon death, then specified mahr is also due in full.
4
Explain the Hanafi reasoning for divorce before consummation
Divorce before consummation entitles the wife to half the specified mahr (Quran 2:237). The commentator notes that seclusion is equivalent to consummation; if seclusion occurred, full mahr would be due.
This prevents injustice: the wife endured the marriage contract and its disruption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقل من عشرة فلها عشرة [۱۸۰ (۵۵) ومن سمى مهرا عشرة فما زاد فعليه المسمى ان دخل بها او مات عنها ۱۸۱ (۵) فان طلقها قبل الدخول والخلوة فلها نصف الصداق و جواز کو نہ تعلیم قرآن الخ ص ۴۵۷ نمبر ۱۴۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ازواج مطہرات کا مہر پانچ سو درہم تھا۔ ایک درہم 0.262 تولہ کا ہوتا ہے یا 3.061 گرام کا ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ان کو پانچ سو سے ضرب دیں تو 131.25 یا 1530.5 گرام چاندی
ہوگی۔ حساب اس طرح ہے۔ 0.262x500 برابر 131.25 تولہ چاندی مہر فاطمی ہوگا۔
500 x 3.061 برابر 1530.50 گرام چاندی مہر فاطمی ہوگا۔
وں روپے یا پاؤنڈ کا حساب خود لگا لیں۔
[۱۷۸۰] (۵۵) کسی نے متعین کیا مہر دس درہم یا اس سے زیادہ تو اس پر متعین کردہ مہر ہے اگر اس سے صحبت کی یا شوہر مر گیا۔ دس درہم یا اسے زیادہ مہرتی ہے تو ہر ی دینا مہر لازم یہ اس ہے کہ کی ہویا دس درہم یا اس سے زیادہ مہر متعین ہے تو اب مہر متعین ہی دینا ہوگا۔ مہر مثل لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ اس صورت میں ہے کہ محبت کی ہویا
پھر صحبت سے پہلے دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کا انتقال ہو گیا ہو۔
صحبت کی تو گویا کہ اپنا مال وصول کیا اس لئے اس کی قیمت یعنی مہر دینا ہوگا۔ اسی طرح صحبت سے پہلے انتقال ہو گیا تو ایک معاملہ طے ہو گیا اس لئے اب پورا مہر ادا کرنا ہوگا آدھا مہر نہیں (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد الله ابن مسعود في رجل تزوج امرأة فمات عنها ولم يدخل بها ولم يفرض لها الصداق؟ فقال لها الصداق كاملا وعليها العدة ولها الميراث قال معقل
بن سنان سمعت رسول الله قضى به في بروع بنت واشق (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فیمن تزوج ولم یسم لها صدا قا حتی مات ص ۲۹۵ نمبر ۲۱۱۴ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل يتزوج المرأة فيموت عنها قبل ان يفرض لها ص ۲۱۷، نمبر ۱۴۵ رستن للبیہقی ، باب احد الزوجین بموت ولم يفرض لها صدا قا ولم يدخل بهاج سابع ج ۱۳۹۹ نمبر ۱۴۱) اس حدیث میں صحبت سے پہلے انتقال ہوا تو پورا مہر دلوایا۔ اس لئے محبت سے پہلے انتقال ہو جائے تو پورا مہر دلوایا جائے گا۔
۱۷۸۱) (۵۶) اور اگر بیوی کی محبت سے پہلے یا خلوت سے پہلے طلاق دی تو اس کے لئے متعین کردہ مہر سے آدھا ہوگا۔ نکاح کیا لیکن ابھی اس کے ساتھ صحبت نہیں کی یا خلوت نہیں کی ۔ کیونکہ خلوت بھی ہمارے یہاں محبت کے درجے میں ہے۔ اور طلاق دے دی تو عورت کے لئے آدھا مہر ہوگا۔ شادی ہو چکی ہے اور اس کو طلاق دے کر متوحش کیا اس لئے عورت کو کچھ نہ کچھ ملنا چاہئے۔ لیکن عورت کا مال سالم واپس گیا ہے اس لئے
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود سے روایت ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے ایک عورت سے شادی کی ۔ پس وہ مرگیا اور عورت سے صحبت نہیں کی اور نہ اس کے لئے مہر متعین کیا تو حضرت نے فرمایا عورت کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا۔ اور اس پر عدت ہوگی۔ اور عورت کے لئے میراث ہوگی۔ حضرت معقل بن سنان نے فرمایا، میں نے حضور سے سنا ہے کہ انہوں بروع بنت واشق کے بارے میں ایساہی فیصلہ فرمایا۔
If [the mahr] is less than ten, she gets ten. [180 (55)] And whoever specifies a mahr of ten or more, then the specified mahr is binding upon him if he consummates the marriage or if he dies. [181 (5)] And if he divorces her before consummation and seclusion, then she gets half of the dower. (and the permissibility of teaching Quran etc. p 457 no 1426) From this hadith it is known that the mahr of the pure wives was five hundred dirhams. One dirham is 0.262 tola or 3.061 grams. So multiply them by five hundred to get 131.25 tola or 1530.5 grams of silver. The calculation is: 0.262 x 500 = 131.25 tola silver, that is the Fatimi mahr. 500 x 3.061 = 1530.50 grams silver, that is the Fatimi mahr. Calculate in rupees or pounds yourself. [1780] (55) If someone specifies a mahr of ten dirhams or more, then the specified mahr is upon him if he has had intercourse with her or if the husband died. Ten dirhams or more is the specified mahr, now he must give the specified mahr. The mahr al-mithl will not be binding. But this is in the case that he had intercourse or if before intercourse one of them died. If he had intercourse, it is as if he received his property, so he must give its price, i.e., the mahr. Similarly, if death occurs before intercourse, the contract is finalized, so the full mahr must be paid, not half. Proof of this is in a hadith: from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud concerning a man who married a woman and died without having intercourse and without specifying a dower. He said: 'For her is the full dower, and she must observe the waiting period, and she inherits.' Ma'qil ibn Sinan said: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah decide similarly regarding Barwa' bint Washiq.' (Abu Dawud... Tirmidhi... Bayhaqi) In this hadith, when death occurred before intercourse, the full mahr was given. Therefore, if death occurs before intercourse, the full mahr is given. [1781] (56) And if he divorces his wife before intercourse or before seclusion, then for her is half of the specified mahr. He married but has not yet had intercourse or seclusion with her. Because seclusion is in the same rank as intercourse in our school. And he divorced her, so the woman gets half the mahr. The marriage took place and he divorced her, so the woman should receive something. But her wealth returns intact, so... Footnote: (alif) From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: A man married a woman, then he died without having intercourse and without specifying a dower. He said: 'For her is the full dower, and she must observe the waiting period, and she inherits.' Ma'qil ibn Sinan said: 'I heard the Prophet decide similarly regarding Barwa' bint Washiq.'
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on what happens when a mahr is specified in the marriage contract. It first reminds that if the specified mahr is less than ten dirhams, the woman still gets ten dirhams because of the minimum. Then it states the main ruling: if the mahr is specified as ten dirhams or more, that specified amount becomes binding (lazim) upon two conditions: either consummation (dukhul) or death of either spouse. This means once the marriage is consummated, the full specified mahr is due. Similarly, if one of the spouses dies before consummation, the full specified mahr is also due. The commentator explains the reasoning: in the case of death, the contract is considered complete, so the full mahr is payable, not half. He supports this with the famous hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq, where the Prophet decided that a woman whose husband died before consummation without specifying a mahr was entitled to the full mahr al-mithl. By analogy, if a mahr was specified, it is due in full. Then the next ruling: if the husband divorces his wife before consummation and before valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah), then she is entitled to half of the specified mahr. Seclusion is treated like actual intercourse in Hanafi law regarding the completion of the mahr. The commentator notes that after divorce before consummation, the woman deserves something (half the mahr) because she endured the disruption of marriage, but since she did not 'deliver' the vulva (the subject of the contract), she only gets half. The footnote repeats the Barwa' hadith for emphasis. Thus, these rulings clarify the consequences of specified mahr: full upon consummation or death, half upon divorce before consummation.

Key Terms
دخول (dukhul): Actual sexual intercourse between spouses.
خلوة (khalwah): Valid seclusion where the spouses are alone in a place where intercourse is not prevented by legal or physical barriers.
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower, i.e., the amount equivalent to the mahr of women similar to the wife (by family, status, etc.), given when no mahr is specified or the specified mahr is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How much mahr is due if a husband divorces his wife before consummation?
A) Full mahr
B) Half of the specified mahr
C) Nothing
D) Mahr al-mithl

Key Takeaway
The specified mahr is fully binding upon consummation or death; half is due upon divorce before consummation.

Ruling on Specified Mahr: Minimum and Full Payment
States the ruling when mahr is specified as less than ten or ten or more

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specified mahr (less than ten vs ten or more) and apply the ruling to scenarios including consummation and death.

Core Idea
Specified mahr less than ten is raised to ten; specified mahr ten or more is binding in full upon intercourse or death.

This lesson addresses two key questions: What happens if a husband specifies a mahr of less than ten dirhams? And what happens if he specifies ten or more? The Hanafi school provides clear rulings based on the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq, establishing the minimum mahr and the binding nature of the specified amount upon consummation or death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal act (specifying mahr in a marriage contract) and the overall hukm (payment of mahr is wajib upon consummation or death).
This is a financial obligation that becomes binding upon certain events.
2
Distinguish the two cases by amount
Separate the scenario where the specified mahr is less than ten dirhams from where it is ten dirhams or more. The ruling differs: less than ten raises to ten; ten or more is binding as specified.
The minimum of ten dirhams is a Hanafi specific ruling.
3
Apply the consequence based on event
For each case, determine the amount due upon consummation (dukhul) or death of either spouse. In both cases, the full mahr (specified or minimum) is due.
If divorce occurs before consummation, the ruling is different (half mahr), but that is not covered here.
4
Connect to the dalil
Examine the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq. It establishes that even without specification, full mahr is due upon death. This implies that when mahr is specified, it is even more binding.
The hadith is cited as proof (dalil) for the full payment upon death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقل من عشرة فلها عشرة ومن سمى مهرا عشرة فما زاد فعليه المسمى ان دخل بها او مات عنها و جواز کو نہ تعلیم قرآن الخ ص ۴۵۷ نمبر ۱۴۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ازواج مطہرات کا مہر پانچ سو درہم تھا۔ ایک درہم 0.262 تولہ کا ہوتا ہے یا 3.061 گرام کا ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ان کو پانچ سو سے ضرب دیں تو 131.25 یا 1530.5 گرام چاندی ہوگی۔ حساب اس طرح ہے۔ 0.262x500 برابر 131.25 تولہ چاندی مہر فاطمی ہوگا۔ 500 x 3.061 برابر 1530.50 گرام چاندی مہر فاطمی ہوگا۔وں روپے یا پاؤنڈ کا حساب خود لگا لیں۔ [۱۷۸۰] (۵۵) کسی نے متعین کیا مہر دس درہم یا اس سے زیادہ تو اس پر متعین کردہ مہر ہے اگر اس سے صحبت کی یا شوہر مر گیا۔ دس درہم یا اسے زیادہ مہرتی ہے تو ہر ی دینا مہر لازم یہ اس ہے کہ کی ہویا دس درہم یا اس سے زیادہ مہر متعین ہے تو اب مہر متعین ہی دینا ہوگا۔ مہر مثل لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ اس صورت میں ہے کہ محبت کی ہویا پھر صحبت سے پہلے دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کا انتقال ہو گیا ہو۔ صحبت کی تو گویا کہ اپنا مال وصول کیا اس لئے اس کی قیمت یعنی مہر دینا ہوگا۔ اسی طرح صحبت سے پہلے انتقال ہو گیا تو ایک معاملہ طے ہو گیا اس لئے اب پورا مہر ادا کرنا ہوگا آدھا مہر نہیں (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن عبد الله ابن مسعود في رجل تزوج امرأة فمات عنها ولم يدخل بها ولم يفرض لها الصداق؟ فقال لها الصداق كاملا وعليها العدة ولها الميراث قال معقل بن سنان سمعت رسول الله قضى به في بروع بنت واشق (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فیمن تزوج ولم یسم لها صدا قا حتی مات ص ۲۹۵ نمبر ۲۱۱۴ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل يتزوج المرأة فيموت عنها قبل ان يفرض لها ص ۲۱۷، نمبر ۱۴۵ رستن للبیہقی ، باب احد الزوجین بموت ولم يفرض لها صدا قا ولم يدخل بهاج سابع ج ۱۳۹۹ نمبر ۱۴۱) اس حدیث میں صحبت سے پہلے انتقال ہوا تو پورا مہر دلوایا۔ اس لئے محبت سے پہلے انتقال ہو جائے تو پورا مہر دلوایا جائے گا۔
If less than ten, then she has ten. And whoever specifies a mahr of ten dirhams or more, then upon him is what he specified if he entered upon her or died upon her. (Urdu: From this hadith it is known that the mahr of the pure wives was five hundred dirhams. One dirham is 0.262 tola or 3.061 grams. So multiply by five hundred to get 131.25 tola or 1530.5 grams of silver. The calculation is thus: ... [1780] (55) Someone specified a mahr of ten dirhams or more, then upon him is the specified mahr if he had intercourse with her or the husband died. ... If intercourse occurred, it is as if he received his property, so its value i.e., the mahr must be given. Similarly, if death occurred before intercourse, a transaction was finalized, so the full mahr must be paid, not half. (2) There is proof of this in the hadith: from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud concerning a man who married a woman and died upon her without entering and without specifying a dower? He said: She gets the full dower, and upon her is the waiting period, and she gets inheritance. Ma'qil ibn Sinan said: I heard the Messenger of God (ﷺ) judged accordingly regarding Barwa' bint Washiq. (Sources: Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Bayhaqi) In this hadith, death occurred before intercourse, so the full mahr was given. Therefore, if death occurs before intercourse, the full mahr will be given.)
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage states two rulings regarding the specification of mahr in a marriage contract. First, if the husband specifies a mahr of less than ten dirhams, the wife is entitled to ten dirhams as the minimum mahr according to the Hanafi school. Second, if he specifies a mahr of ten dirhams or more, then he is obliged to pay the specified amount upon consummation of the marriage or upon the death of either spouse. The commentary explains that in both cases, the full specified mahr is due because intercourse or death finalizes the contract, making the mahr a binding debt. The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud about Barwa' bint Washiq is cited as proof that even without specification, full mahr is due upon death; a fortiori when it is specified. The passage also provides a calculation of the mahr fatimi (the standard mahr of the Prophet's household) as five hundred dirhams, equivalent to approximately 131.25 tola or 1530.5 grams of silver.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower or bridal gift that a husband is obligated to pay to the wife as a condition of the marriage contract.
دخول (dukhul): Actual sexual intercourse between the spouses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 8 dirhams
B) 4 dirhams (half)
C) 10 dirhams (minimum)
D) No mahr, only inheritance

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets a minimum mahr of ten dirhams; any specified mahr below that is raised to ten, and any specified mahr of ten or more is binding in full upon consummation or death.

Ruling on Half Mahr Upon Divorce Before Consummation
States that if divorce occurs before consummation, half the specified mahr is due, with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr upon divorce before consummation, cite the Quranic proof, and explain the legal effect of khalwah.

Core Idea
Divorce before consummation entitles the wife to half the specified mahr, as commanded in Quran 2:237.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in marriage: what happens to the mahr if the husband divorces his wife before the marriage is consummated? The Hanafi school, relying on a clear Quranic verse, rules that the wife receives half of the agreed-upon mahr. We will also explore the concept of khalwah (valid seclusion), which in Hanafi fiqh is equivalent to consummation for mahr purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific act being ruled upon (divorce before consummation/khalwah) and the resulting hukm (half mahr due).
The ruling is wajib, as derived from the Quranic imperative.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence cited: Quran 2:237. Note that it is a direct, unambiguous text (qat'i al-thubut wa al-dalalah).
No other school disputes the authenticity of this verse.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the verse proves the ruling. The word 'fanishf' (فنصف) is an imperative, indicating obligation in Hanafi usul.
The verse explicitly states 'half of what you have appointed'.
4
Consider the effect of khalwah
Understand that in Hanafi fiqh, valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) is treated like actual consummation for mahr and iddah. If khalwah occurred before divorce, full mahr is due.
This is a distinctive Hanafi ruling; other schools may not equate khalwah with consummation.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
Recognize that there is no significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this matter. The ruling is part of Zahir al-Riwayah and is universally accepted in the school.
The footnote in the text cites a related hadith about full mahr upon death, which reinforces the principle by contrast.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان طلقها قبل الدخول والخلوة فلها نصف الصداق [۱۷۸۱] (۵۶) اور اگر بیوی کی محبت سے پہلے یا خلوت سے پہلے طلاق دی تو اس کے لئے متعین کردہ مہر سے آدھا ہوگا۔ نکاح کیا لیکن ابھی اس کے ساتھ صحبت نہیں کی یا خلوت نہیں کی ۔ کیونکہ خلوت بھی ہمارے یہاں محبت کے درجے میں ہے۔ اور طلاق دے دی تو عورت کے لئے آدھا مہر ہوگا۔ شادی ہو چکی ہے اور اس کو طلاق دے کر متوحش کیا اس لئے عورت کو کچھ نہ کچھ ملنا چاہئے۔ لیکن عورت کا مال سالم واپس گیا ہے اس لئے پورا مہر نہیں ملے گا بلکہ آدھا مہر ملے گا (۲) آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ وان طلقتموهن من قبل ان تمسوهن وقد فرضتم لهن فريضة فنصف ما فرضتم الا ان يعفون او يعفو الذي بيده عقدة النكاح (الف ) ( آیت ۲۳۷ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ صحبت سے پہلے طلاق دے تو عورت کو آدھا مہر ملے گا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود سے روایت ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے ایک عورت سے شادی کی ۔ پس وہ مرگیا اور عورت سے صحبت نہیں کی اور نہ اس کے لئے مہر متعین کیا تو حضرت نے فرمایا عورت کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا۔ اور اس پر عدت ہوگی۔ اور عورت کے لئے میراث ہوگی۔ حضرت معقل بن سنان نے فرمایا، میں نے حضور سے سنا ہے کہ انہوں بروع بنت واشق کے بارے میں ایساہی فیصلہ فرمایا۔
So if he divorces her before entering (dukhul) and seclusion (khalwah), then she gets half of the dower. [1781] (56) And if he divorces her before intercourse or seclusion, then she gets half of the specified mahr. ... The proof is in the verse: 'And if you divorce them before you have touched them and you have appointed for them an obligation, then half of what you have appointed, unless they forgo or the one in whose hand is the knot of marriage forgoes.' (2:237) This verse states that if divorce is given before intercourse, the wife gets half the mahr. Footnote (a): From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: a man married a woman and died before entering and without specifying a dower; he said she gets the full dower, waiting period, and inheritance. Ma'qil ibn Sinan heard the Prophet (ﷺ) judged similarly regarding Barwa' bint Washiq.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage establishes the well-known principle that if a husband divorces his wife before consummating the marriage (or before valid seclusion, which in the Hanafi school is equivalent to consummation), the wife is entitled to half of the specified mahr. The commentary explains the rationale: since the marriage contract was valid but the wife's 'goods' (i.e., her person) have not been fully utilized, she receives half as compensation. The Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:237) is cited as direct proof, where the command to give half the appointed dower is explicit. The footnote reiterates the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq, though that hadith pertains to death, not divorce; it is included as supporting evidence for the principle that the full mahr is due upon death, in contrast to divorce which yields half.

Key Terms
خلوة (khalwah): Valid seclusion between a married couple without impediments, which in Hanafi fiqh is considered equivalent to consummation for purposes of mahr and iddah.
نصف الصداق (nisf al-sadaq): Half of the specified dower, due to the wife upon divorce before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 500 dirhams
C) 250 dirhams
D) No mahr

Key Takeaway
Upon divorce before consummation or khalwah, half the specified mahr is wajib, as directly commanded in the Quran.

Mahr al-Mithl: When No Mahr Is Specified – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
States the Hanafi ruling and dispute on mahr al-mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mahr al-mithl when no mahr is specified, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate which evidence is stronger according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A marriage without a specified mahr still obligates mahr al-mithl; the dispute hinges on prophetic hadith vs. companion athar.

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that when a marriage contract lacks a specified mahr or even explicitly states 'no mahr,' the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers) upon consummation or death of the husband. The commentary then introduces the Shafi'i objection: that upon death before consummation, no mahr is due. By tracing the proofs from both schools, we will see how the Hanafis prioritize a prophetic hadith over a companion statement to uphold the obligation of mahr.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its conditions
Identify the act (marriage without specified mahr) and the ruling: mahr al-mithl is wajib. Note that the obligation applies whether consummation occurred or the husband died.
The condition that triggers mahr al-mithl is either consummation or death of the husband—both finalize the contract's implied mahr.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees specifically on the death-before-consummation scenario. He argues that the wife receives inheritance only, not mahr.
The disagreement is limited to death before consummation; both schools likely agree on consummation triggering mahr al-mithl.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i rely on the athar (companion narration) from Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'She has inheritance and no dower.' Understand that this is a qawl al-sahabi, considered a valid but weaker source compared to marfu' hadith in Hanafi usul.
The Hanafis do accept qawl al-sahabi as evidence, but they give precedence to a prophetic hadith when both exist.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the prophetic hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (endorsed by the Prophet) is stronger in transmission and more specific; it directly addresses the case of death without specified mahr and grants mahr al-mithl.
The hadith is a single narration (ahad), but its meaning (dalala) is clear and definitive. The athar of Ali may be interpreted as negating a specified mahr, not mahr al-mithl.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, a widow whose husband died before consummation without specified mahr receives both inheritance and mahr al-mithl. Under Shafi'i law, she receives inheritance only.
This difference can have significant financial implications for the widow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان تزوجها ولم يسم لها مهرا او تزوجها على ان لا مهر لها فلها مهر مثلها ان دخل بها او مات عنها [۱۷۸۲] (۵۷) اور اگر شادی کی اور عورت کے لئے مہر متعین نہیں کیا ، یا شادی کی اس شرط پر کہ عورت کے لئے مہر نہیں ہوگا تو اس کے لئے مہر مثل ہے اگر اس سے صحبت کی یا انتقال کر گیا۔ عورت سے شادی کی اور شادی کے وقت مہر متعین نہیں کیا، یا یوں کہا کہ تمہارے لئے مہر نہیں ہے تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں اگر صحبت کی تب بھی مہر مثل ملے گا یا مرد کا انتقال ہو جائے تب بھی عورت کو مہر مثل ملے گا۔ اگر مہر متعین نہ کیا ہوا اور صحبت کرے تو مہر مثل لازم ہوتا ہے۔ عن ابن مسعود انه سئل عن رجل تزوج امرأة ولم يفرض لها صداقا ولم يدخل بها حتى مات فقال ابن مسعود لها مثل صداق نسائها لا وكس ولا شطط وعيلها العدة ولها الميراث فقام معقل ابن سنان الاشجعي فقال قضى رسول الله فى بروع بنت واشق امرأة منا مثل ما قضيت ففرح بها ابن مسعود (ب) ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الرجل يتزوج المرأة فيموت عنها قبل ان يفرض لها ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۱۱۴۵ را بو داؤد شریف، باب فیمن تزوج ولم یسم لها صدا قامتی مات ص ۲۹۵ نمبر ۲۱۱۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مہر متعین نہ کیا ہو اور شوہر کا انتقال ہو جائے تو عورت کے لئے مہر مثل ہوگا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ چونکہ مہر متعین نہیں ہے اور انتقال ہو گیا تو عورت کو کچھ بھی نہیں ملے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن علی قال فی المتوفى عنها ولم يفرض لها صداقا لها الميراث ولا صداق لها (ج) (سنن سیقی ، باب من قال لا صداق بھاج سابع ص ۴۰۳، نمبر ۱۴۴۲۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ایسی عورت کو مہر نہیں ملے گا۔
And if he marries her and does not specify a mahr for her, or marries her on the condition that there is no mahr for her, then she gets the mahr of her peers (mahr al-mithl) if he enters upon her or dies upon her. [1782] (57) ... The hadith says that when no mahr was specified and the husband dies, the woman gets mahr al-mithl. Imam Shafi'i says that because no mahr was specified and death occurred, she gets nothing. Their proof is the narration from Ali: 'For a woman whose husband died without specifying a dower, she gets inheritance and no dower.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position that when a marriage contract is concluded without specification of mahr or with an explicit condition that there be no mahr, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers) upon consummation or the death of either spouse. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud concerning Barwa' bint Washiq, where the Prophet (ﷺ) ruled that she gets the mahr of her peers. The commentary then records the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that upon death without consummation, the wife receives no mahr at all, only inheritance. His evidence is the narration from Ali (رضي الله عنه) that in such a case, she has no mahr. The Hanafi school prefers the explicit hadith over the athar of Ali, and also uses qiyas: since the contract entails mahr by implication, death finalizes it, so mahr must be paid.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr equivalent to that given to women of similar status (family, beauty, education, etc.) in the wife's community, used when no mahr is specified.
اثر (athar): A narration from a Companion (here, Ali ibn Abi Talib) used as a source of law in the Hanafi school, though it is considered weaker than a marfu' hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on mahr if a man marries a woman and explicitly states 'no mahr for you,' and then dies before consummation?
A) The condition stands; she gets no mahr.
B) She gets half of mahr al-mithl.
C) She gets full mahr al-mithl.
D) The marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is wajib upon consummation or death in a marriage without a specified mahr, and Hanafis uphold this with a prophetic hadith over a companion athar.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Mut'ah (Gift) Upon Divorce Before Consummation When No Mahr Specified
Ruling statement with footnote elaboration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for mut'ah when a woman is divorced before consummation with no specified mahr, and identify the amount and conditions.

Core Idea
If divorce occurs before consummation and no mahr was specified, the wife receives a wajib gift of three garments.

This lesson addresses a specific situation in marriage: a man divorces his wife before any physical intimacy and without having specified a dower. In such a case, the wife is not entitled to half of a specified mahr (since none was specified), but she does not leave empty-handed. The Hanafi school rules that she must receive a consolatory gift called mut'ah, consisting of three garments, based on Quranic guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving mut'ah (consolatory gift) to the divorced wife. Its ruling is wajib (obligatory) in this specific scenario.
Wajib means it must be fulfilled; omission is a sin.
2
Identify the conditions
The conditions for mut'ah are: (1) divorce occurs before consummation or valid seclusion, and (2) no mahr (dower) was specified in the marriage contract.
If a mahr was specified, the wife gets half of it, not mut'ah.
3
Note the specific amount
According to the Hanafi school, the mut'ah consists of three garments. This is the standard amount from the reliable transmissions.
The value may vary based on the husband's wealth, but the school fixes it at three garments.
4
Understand the evidential basis
The primary evidence is Quran 2:236, which commands giving a gift to divorced women when no mahr was specified and before consummation. The Hanafi school interprets this as an obligation (wajib).
Other schools may see it as recommended (mandub).
5
Distinguish from the death case
The footnote mentions the case of death before consummation with no mahr, where the wife gets full mahr, inheritance, and iddah. This is a different ruling—mut'ah only applies to divorce, not death.
Do not confuse the two scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۷۸۳] (۵۸) اور اگر اس کو طلاق دی اس سے صحبت سے پہلے، یا خلوت سے پہلے تو اس کے لئے متعہ ہوگا۔ اور متعہ تین کپڑے ہیں اس کی حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود سے روایت ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے ایک عورت سے شادی کی ۔ پس وہ مرگیا اور عورت سے صحبت نہیں کی اور نہ اس کے لئے مہر متعین کیا تو حضرت نے فرمایا عورت کے لئے پورا مہر ہوگا۔ اور اس پر عدت ہوگی۔ اور عورت کے لئے میراث ہوگی۔ حضرت معقل بن سنان نے فرمایا، میں نے حضور سے سنا ہے کہ انہوں بروع بنت واشق کے بارے میں ایساہی فیصلہ فرمایا۔
[1783] (58) And if he divorces her before intercourse, or before seclusion, then for her is a mut'ah (gift). And the mut'ah is three garments. Footnote (a): From Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: a man married a woman and died before entering and without specifying a dower; he said she gets the full dower, waiting period, and inheritance. Ma'qil ibn Sinan heard the Prophet (ﷺ) judged similarly regarding Barwa' bint Washiq.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a case where a woman is divorced before consummation and no mahr was specified. In such a situation, she is not entitled to half of a specified mahr (since none was specified), but she receives a symbolic gift called mut'ah. The Hanafi school specifies that this mut'ah consists of three garments. The footnote repeats the hadith of Barwa', which actually deals with death, not divorce; it is included as general support for the principle that a woman is not left empty-handed. The ruling on mut'ah is based on the Quranic verse (2:236) which says 'give them a gift, the wealthy according to his means and the poor according to his means'.

Key Terms
متعہ (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a divorced woman, especially when no mahr was specified and divorce occurs before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man marries a woman without specifying any mahr, then divorces her before consummation. What is she entitled to?
A) Half of mahr al-mithl
B) Full mahr al-mithl
C) Three garments as mut'ah
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
When a woman is divorced before consummation with no mahr specified, she must receive a consolatory gift of three garments (mut'ah) in the Hanafi school.
